Refuting the Qadariyya on divine power over compulsion
Al-Ash'ari argues that if God cannot compel faith, weakness results.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses conditional reasoning to show that denying God's power to compel faith logically entails attributing weakness to God, and that the Qadariyya position forces them to deny divine omnipotence.

Core Idea
Denying God's power to compel faith leads to the absurd conclusion that God is weak.

This passage presents a powerful logical argument against the Qadariyya (Mu'tazila) who affirm human free will to the extent that God cannot compel belief. Al-Ash'ari shows that if God cannot make people believe, then He is powerless to achieve His will—a clear contradiction with His omnipotence. Understanding this argument helps clarify the Islamic doctrine of divine power and its relationship to human actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic carefully, then the translation. Notice the conditional structure and the key terms like 'compulsion' (iljā') and 'power' (qudra).
2
Identify the two parts of the argument
The passage consists of a conditional argument (if no power to compel then weakness) and a dilemma for the Qadariyya (if humans can always disbelieve, God cannot guarantee faith). Mark these two sections.
The first part uses 'فكما... فكذلك' (just as... similarly).
3
Analyze the logical necessity
Ask yourself: why does inability to compel imply weakness? Al-Ash'ari argues that if something you don't will happens, you are weak; if you cannot make what you will happen, you are also weak. This is a necessary rational judgment.
4
Connect to the Qadariyya position
See how the argument refutes the Qadariyya: they claim humans have power to believe or disbelieve even under compelling signs, so God cannot make them believe inevitably. This leads to denying God's power over that matter, which is absurd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فكما يَجِبُ بكون ما لا يريده الضعف والوهن والتقصير عن بلوغ ما يريده، لو لم يوصف بالقدرة على أن يُلجئهم إلى ذلك، فكذلك يَجِبُ له الضعف والوهَنُ والتقصير عن بلوغ ما يريده، إذا أرادَ كونه على وجه لا يُوصَف بالقدرة على وقوعِهِ على ذلك الوجه . وأيضًا فإنَّه يَلزَمُ القدرية - إِذَا كَانَ مَنْ قَدَرَ أَنْ يُؤمِنَ قَدَرَ أن يَكفُرَ - أَنْ لا يكون الباري -تعالى- موصوفًا بالقُدرَةِ على الأمرِ، الذي لو فعله لكانوا مؤمنين لا محالة؛ لأنَّهم يقدِرُونَ - عِندَهم على أن يكفروا ، عند نزولِ الآياتِ المُلْجِيَّاتِ إلى الإيمان، كما يقدرون أن يؤمنوا قبل ذلك ، ومَنْ قدَرَ على الكفر عندَ نزول الآيةِ لم يُؤْمَنْ وقوعه منه .
Just as weakness, feebleness, and falling short of attaining what He wills must be necessarily implied by the occurrence of what He does not will, if He were not described as having power to compel them to that, similarly weakness, feebleness, and falling short of attaining what He wills must be necessarily implied for Him if He wills something to occur in a manner in which He is not described as having power for its occurrence upon that manner. And also, it necessarily follows for the Qadariyya—since whoever has the power to believe has the power to disbelieve—that the Exalted Creator is not described as having power over the matter which, if He did it, they would inevitably be believers; because they, according to them, have the power to disbelieve at the descent of the compelling signs (al-āyāt al-muljiʾāt) to faith, just as they have the power to believe before that. And whoever has the power to disbelieve at the descent of the sign, his occurrence (of disbelief) is not to be deemed impossible.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a proof against the Qadariyya (Mu'tazila) who affirm human free will to choose belief or unbelief, thereby denying that God can compel them to faith. Al-Ash'ari uses a conditional argument: if having something occur that one does not will implies weakness and inability to attain what one wills, then if God were not described as having power to compel (yulji') them to what He wills, He would be subject to weakness. But God is not subject to weakness, so He must have such power. Then he poses a dilemma for the Qadariyya: they claim humans have power to both believe and disbelieve. Therefore, even if God were to send compelling signs (miracles that necessarily produce faith), humans would still have the power to disbelieve, so their faith would not be guaranteed. Thus God would lack power over making them believers, which is absurd. The argument shows that the Qadariyya position forces them to deny God's omnipotence in order to preserve human free will.

Key Terms
قدرية
إلجاء
قدرة
آيات ملجئات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying God's power to compel faith is a minor point that doesn't affect God's power.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari demonstrates that it logically entails attributing weakness and inability to God, contradicting His omnipotence.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Ash'ari argue that the Qadariyya position leads to God not being described as having power over the matter?
A) Because they claim humans have power to disbelieve even when compelled
B) Because they deny God's existence
C) Because they say God cannot create evil
D) Because they affirm human responsibility

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari proves that denying God's power to compel faith leads to the absurdity of divine weakness, refuting the Qadariyya.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God has absolute power over your faith, or do you secretly think your own will is stronger? If you believe God could compel you to believe, why do you still struggle with doubt?
?
Al-Ash'ari says denying God's power to compel leads to attributing weakness to Him. Have you ever, in your heart, thought that God is not fully in control of your choices? What does that say about your understanding of His attributes?
?
If God sent a clear sign forcing you to believe, would you still find a way to disbelieve? What does that reveal about your reliance on your own will versus His power, and are you content with that reliance?

God Creates Our Actions: A Quranic Proof and Objection
Ash'ari proves servants' actions are created by God and answers an objection about the interpretation of 'خلقكم وما تعملون'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ash'ari's Quranic proof that human actions are created by God and his refutation of the objection that the verse 'وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ' refers to idols rather than deeds.

Core Idea
God's creation of our actions is proven by the recompense due for them.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari tackles a central question of qadar: Are our actions created by God? He provides a clear Quranic proof and then anticipates a potential misinterpretation of the key verse. This lesson walks through his argument and his response to the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Ash'ari uses a very compact style, combining proof and objection.
2
Identify the proof and its logic
Find the two Quranic verses Ash'ari cites. Understand how the recompense verse (56:24) supports the claim that actions are created by God.
The logic is: recompense is for actions, recompense is from God, therefore actions are created by God.
3
Examine the objection and refutation
Read the objector's statement and Ash'ari's response. See how he distinguishes between the verse about idols and the verse about actions.
The refutation hinges on the fact that the idols are carved by them, so the carving verse is about idols, not about their general actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في القدر
إن قال قائل: لم زعمتم أن أكساب العباد مخلوقة لله تعالى؟ قيل له: قلنا ذلك؛ لأن الله تعالى قال: {وَاللَّهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ} [الصافات:96]، وقال: {جَزَاءً بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ} [الواقعة:24]، فلما كان الجزاء واقعًا على أعمالهم، كان الخالق لأعمالهم.
فإن قال: أليس الله تعالى قال: {قَالَ أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ} [الصافات:95]، وعنى الأصنام التي نحتوها، فما أنكرتم أن يكون قوله: {خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ} أراد به الأصنام التي عملوها؟
قيل له: خطأ ما ظننته؛ لأن الأصنام منحوتة لهم في الحقيقة، فرجع الله تعالى بقوله: {أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ} إليها، وليست [؟]
Chapter: Speech on Predestination. If a questioner says: Why do you claim that the acquisitions of servants are created by God Almighty? It is said to him: We say that because God Almighty said: 'And God created you and what you do' [37:96], and He said: 'A recompense for what they used to do' [56:24]. So when recompense is based on their actions, then He is the Creator of their actions. If he says: Did not God Almighty say: 'He said: Do you worship what you carve?' [37:95], meaning the idols they carved; so why do you not deny that His saying: 'He created you and what you do' meant the idols which they made? It is said to him: You are mistaken in what you thought; because the idols are indeed carved by them, so God Almighty's saying: 'Do you worship what you carve' refers to them, and they are not [؟]
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a combined proof-and-objection section. Ash'ari begins by stating the claim that servants' acquisitions (أكساب العباد) are created by God. He provides a Quranic proof from Sūrat al-Ṣāffāt (37:96): 'And God created you and what you do.' He then adds Sūrat al-Wāqiʿa (56:24): 'A recompense for what they used to do.' The reasoning is that since recompense (جزاء) is given for actions, and recompense is from God, the actions themselves must be created by God (otherwise the recompense would be for something not created by Him). An objector then raises a potential misinterpretation: could the verse 'created you and what you do' refer to the idols they make rather than their actions? He cites the nearby verse 'Do you worship what you carve?' to support this reading. Ash'ari refutes this by noting that the idols are indeed carved by the people (منحوتة لهم), so the phrase 'what you carve' refers back to the idols, not to their general actions. The verse 'created you and what you do' therefore refers to their deeds, as the recompense verse confirms. The answer is cut off at 'and they are not' (وليست), likely concluding that the idols are not the subject of the creation verse.

Key Terms
أكساب العباد
مخلوقة
خلق
جزاء
أعمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Wa-Allahu khalaqakum wa ma ta'malun' refers to the idols that the polytheists carved.
Correction: Ash'ari shows that the nearby verse 'ata'buduna ma tanhitun' refers to the idols, while the creation verse is about their actions, as confirmed by the recompense verse.

Checkpoint
What is the main proof Ash'ari gives to show that servants' actions are created by God?
A) The verse 'أتعبدون ما تنحتون'
B) The verse 'والله خلقكم وما تعملون' and that recompense is for actions
C) Rational argument that servants cannot create their own actions
D) Consensus of scholars

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari grounds the creation of human actions in the logic of divine recompense and defends the straightforward reading of the Qur'anic text against interpretive objections.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every action you do is created by God, how does that change the way you think about your own choices and responsibilities? When you sin, do you find yourself excusing it by saying 'God willed it'? What does this lesson demand of you instead?
?
The objector in this lesson twisted a clear verse to fit his preconception. Are there any verses or teachings of Islam that you have been tempted to reinterpret to avoid a hard truth about your own life? Will you let the Qur'an correct you, or will you continue to adjust it to your comfort?
?
God's recompense for actions is the proof that He creates them. Do you live as if your smallest deed is seen and will be repaid? Does your daily routine reflect that conviction, or have you grown careless? What will you change starting today to live with that awareness?

Divine Decree

The first objection: Do 'what you do' refer to idols?
Imam Ash'ari presents the first objection and its response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari refutes the claim that the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' refers to idols rather than human actions.

Core Idea
Your actions are created by Allah, not the objects you make.

Imam Ash'ari begins by establishing the foundational proof that human actions are created by Allah, using clear Qur'anic evidence. He then anticipates and answers an objection that might confuse the meaning of 'what you do' with the idols worshipped by the disbelievers. This lesson breaks down his careful reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the objection
Notice how the objector tries to reinterpret the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' as referring to idols, based on another verse about carving idols.
The objector uses a linguistic argument about the phrase 'what you do'.
3
Understand the response
See how Imam Ash'ari distinguishes between the two verses. The verse about carving (37:95) refers to the act of carving, but the verse about creation (37:96) refers to actions because it is linked to recompense.
4
Grasp the key distinction
Recognize that humans do not actually create the wood they carve; they only shape it. So 'what you do' cannot mean the idols, but must mean your deeds.
This is a subtle point about the nature of creation and acquisition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في القدر
[أَفعالُ العِبادِ مِن خَلْقَ الله ]
إن قال قائل : لم زَعمتم أنَّ أَكْسَابَ العبادِ مخلوقةٌ للَّهِ - تعالى - ؟ قِيلَ لَه : قلنا ذلك ؛ لأنَّ اللَّهَ -تعالى- قالَ : وَاللهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات: ٩٦]، وقال: ﴿ جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الواقعة: ٢٤] فلما كان الجزاء واقعا على أعمالهم ، كانَ الخالقَ لأَعْمالِهم .
فإن قالَ : أَفَلَيْس الله -تعالى- قال : قَالَ أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ ﴿قَالَ [الصافات : ٩٥] ، وعَنى الأصنام التي نَحَتُوها ، فما أنكرتُم أن يكونَ قوله : خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ أراد [به] الأصنام التي عَمِلُوها ؟
قِيلَ لَه : خَطَأَ ما ظَنَنْتَهُ؛ لأنَّ الأصنام منحوتة لهم في الحقيقة، فرَجَع الله -تعالى- بقولِهِ : أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ إِلَيْها، وليست الخُشُبُ معمولةٌ لهم في الحقيقة، فيَرْجِع بقولِهِ : خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ إليها
فإن قال قائِل : أليس قد قالَ اللهُ تعالى - : تَلْقَفُ مَا يَأْفِكُونَ [الأعراف: ۱۱۷] ، ولم يُرِد به إِفْكَهم، فما أنكرت أن لا يرجع بقوله : خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ إلى أعمالِهِم؟
قيلَ لَهُ : الذي يَأْفِكُونَ : هو الأَمثِلَةُ التي خَيَّلُوا إِلى الناسِ أَنَّهَا حَيَاتٌ تَسعَى، وإفكُهُم تَخْييلهم؛ فأراد بقوله : يأْفِكُونَ أي يُخيّلونَ إلى الناسِ أنَّها حيَّاتُ تسعى، وإفكُهُمْ هو إيهامُهُمُ الشَّيء على خلافِ ما هو بسَبيله؛ فالأمثلة هي التي يأفكون، ويخيلونَ إلى الناسِ أَنَّها تسعى في الحقيقة، وهيَ الَّتِي تَلْقَفُها العَصا .
وليسَ يجوز أن يَعملُوا الخُشُبَ في الحقيقة، فلمْ يَجُزْ أن يكونَ الله -تعالى- أراد بقوله : ﴿ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ إليها، ووجب أن يَرْجِعَ إلى الأعمالِ، كَما رجَعَ بقوله : جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ إلى الأعمال .
فلو جاز لزاعم أن يَزْعُم أَنَّ قولَ اللَّهِ -تعالى-: ﴿ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا
Chapter on speech about predestination. [Actions of servants are from Allah's creation.] If a speaker says: Why do you claim that the acquisitions of servants are created by Allah, exalted? It is said to him: We said that because Allah, exalted, said: 'And Allah created you and what you do' [Surah as-Saffat 37:96], and He said: 'Recompense for what they used to do' [Surah al-Waqi'ah 56:24]. Since recompense occurs upon their actions, He is the Creator of their actions. If he says: Did not Allah, exalted, say: 'He said, Do you worship what you carve?' [Surah as-Saffat 37:95], meaning the idols which they carved? So what prevents you from thinking that His saying: 'created you and what you do' intended the idols which they made? It is said to him: What you thought is wrong, because the idols are carved by them in reality, but Allah's saying: 'Do you worship what you carve?' refers to them, and the wood is not made by them in reality, so His saying: 'created you and what you do' refers to them. If a speaker says: Did not Allah, exalted, say: 'It swallows what they fabricate' [Surah al-A'raf 7:117], and He did not intend their fabrication? So what prevents you from thinking that His saying: 'created you and what you do' does not refer to their actions? It is said to him: 'What they fabricate' are the ropes which they made to appear to the people as though they were moving snakes, and their fabrication is their making an illusion. So He intended by His saying 'they fabricate' i.e., they make people imagine that they are moving snakes, and their fabrication is their making something appear contrary to what it actually is. So the ropes are what they fabricate and make people imagine that they move in reality, and they are what the staff swallows. And it is not permissible that they actually make the wood, so it is not permissible that Allah, exalted, intended His saying 'created you and what you do' to refer to them, and it is necessary that it refers to actions, just as His saying 'Recompense for what they used to do' refers to actions. So if a claimant were to claim that Allah's saying: 'created you and what you do' ...
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two objections against the doctrine that human actions are created by Allah. The author, Imam Ash'ari, presents the objections and answers them sequentially. The first objection: The objector asks why they claim that human actions (aksab al-ibad) are created by Allah. The answer cites two Qur'anic verses: 'Allah created you and what you do' (37:96) and 'Recompense for what they used to do' (56:24). Since recompense (jaza') is based on actions, the Creator of those actions must be Allah. The objector then raises a second objection: Could the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' refer to the idols that the disbelievers carved, as in the verse 'Do you worship what you carve?' (37:95)? The answer distinguishes between the two verses: 'what you carve' refers to the idols, which are actually carved by humans, but 'what you do' in 37:96 cannot refer to idols because the idols are not 'made' by humans in reality—they are merely carved from pre-existing material. Thus, the verse must refer to their actions. A third objection is presented: In the verse about Prophet Moses' staff swallowing the magicians' ropes (7:117), the phrase 'what they fabricate' (ma ya'fikun) refers to the ropes, not the act of fabrication; so similarly, 'what you do' could refer to something other than actions. The answer explains that 'fabrication' (ifk) here means illusion or deception, not actual creation. The magicians made the ropes appear to be snakes through trickery, but they did not create the ropes; they only made people imagine they were snakes. Therefore, the verse still refers to an action (the act of making illusions), not an object. The passage concludes by stating that if it is not permissible for humans to actually create wood, then the verse cannot refer to the wood, but must refer to actions, consistent with the recompense verse. The text cuts off at the beginning of a new hypothetical objection.

Key Terms
أكْساب العباد
مخلوقة
خلق
أعمال
الأصنام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'Allah created you and what you do' refers to idols that people make.
Correction: The verse refers to human actions, not idols, because recompense is given for actions, and humans do not create the material of idols.

Checkpoint
How does Imam Ash'ari respond to the objection that the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' could refer to idols?
A) He agrees and explains that idols are also created by Allah.
B) He points out that the verse about carving (37:95) refers to idols, while the verse in question refers to actions because recompense is based on actions.
C) He argues that idols are not real creations, so the verse cannot apply to them.
D) He rejects the objection as invalid without explanation.

Key Takeaway
Imam Ash'ari proves that human actions are created by Allah by distinguishing between the act of carving (which humans do) and the creation of the action itself (which is from Allah).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you truly believe that Allah created that action? How does this belief affect the way you repent and seek His forgiveness?
?
If every action is created by Allah, why do you still feel pride in your good deeds? Are you attributing them to yourself, and how should that change your attitude?
?
How does this lesson challenge your tendency to blame others or circumstances for your mistakes? Will you now take full responsibility, knowing that your actions are still your acquisitions (kasb)?

The second objection: Is 'what you do' like 'what they fabricate'?
Imam Ash'ari refutes the second objection using the verse about Moses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Ash'ari responds to the objection that the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' might not refer to actions, by analyzing the verse about the magicians' fabrication.

Core Idea
False analogy: fabricated illusions are not the same as real actions.

The objector tries a second tactic, drawing an analogy from the story of Prophet Moses (peace be upon him) where the phrase 'what they fabricate' refers to the ropes, not the act of fabrication. Imam Ash'ari carefully unpacks the meaning of fabrication (ifk) to show that it actually refers to an action—the act of making illusions—thereby reaffirming that 'what you do' means real actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the second objection and response.
2
Identify the objection
Notice how the objector uses the verse about Moses to argue that 'what you do' could refer to something other than actions, like the idols.
The objector claims that since 'what they fabricate' refers to the ropes, not the act of fabricating, the same could apply to 'what you do'.
3
Understand the response
See how Imam Ash'ari explains that fabrication (ifk) means making illusions, which is itself an action. The ropes are not actually created by the magicians; they only cause people to imagine they are snakes.
Thus, the verse still points to an action of the magicians—their act of deception.
4
Grasp the principle
Recognize the key principle: humans cannot create the material objects they work with; they only modify them. Therefore, 'what you do' cannot refer to the objects but to the actions themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في القدر
[أَفعالُ العِبادِ مِن خَلْقَ الله ]
إن قال قائل : لم زَعمتم أنَّ أَكْسَابَ العبادِ مخلوقةٌ للَّهِ - تعالى - ؟ قِيلَ لَه : قلنا ذلك ؛ لأنَّ اللَّهَ -تعالى- قالَ : وَاللهُ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الصافات: ٩٦]، وقال: ﴿ جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ [الواقعة: ٢٤] فلما كان الجزاء واقعا على أعمالهم ، كانَ الخالقَ لأَعْمالِهم .
فإن قالَ : أَفَلَيْس الله -تعالى- قال : قَالَ أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ ﴿قَالَ [الصافات : ٩٥] ، وعَنى الأصنام التي نَحَتُوها ، فما أنكرتُم أن يكونَ قوله : خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ أراد [به] الأصنام التي عَمِلُوها ؟
قِيلَ لَه : خَطَأَ ما ظَنَنْتَهُ؛ لأنَّ الأصنام منحوتة لهم في الحقيقة، فرَجَع الله -تعالى- بقولِهِ : أَتَعْبُدُونَ مَا تَنْحِتُونَ إِلَيْها، وليست الخُشُبُ معمولةٌ لهم في الحقيقة، فيَرْجِع بقولِهِ : خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ إليها
فإن قال قائِل : أليس قد قالَ اللهُ تعالى - : تَلْقَفُ مَا يَأْفِكُونَ [الأعراف: ۱۱۷] ، ولم يُرِد به إِفْكَهم، فما أنكرت أن لا يرجع بقوله : خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ إلى أعمالِهِم؟
قيلَ لَهُ : الذي يَأْفِكُونَ : هو الأَمثِلَةُ التي خَيَّلُوا إِلى الناسِ أَنَّهَا حَيَاتٌ تَسعَى، وإفكُهُم تَخْييلهم؛ فأراد بقوله : يأْفِكُونَ أي يُخيّلونَ إلى الناسِ أنَّها حيَّاتُ تسعى، وإفكُهُمْ هو إيهامُهُمُ الشَّيء على خلافِ ما هو بسَبيله؛ فالأمثلة هي التي يأفكون، ويخيلونَ إلى الناسِ أَنَّها تسعى في الحقيقة، وهيَ الَّتِي تَلْقَفُها العَصا .
وليسَ يجوز أن يَعملُوا الخُشُبَ في الحقيقة، فلمْ يَجُزْ أن يكونَ الله -تعالى- أراد بقوله : ﴿ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ ﴾ إليها، ووجب أن يَرْجِعَ إلى الأعمالِ، كَما رجَعَ بقوله : جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ إلى الأعمال .
فلو جاز لزاعم أن يَزْعُم أَنَّ قولَ اللَّهِ -تعالى-: ﴿ خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا
Chapter on speech about predestination. [Actions of servants are from Allah's creation.] If a speaker says: Why do you claim that the acquisitions of servants are created by Allah, exalted? It is said to him: We said that because Allah, exalted, said: 'And Allah created you and what you do' [Surah as-Saffat 37:96], and He said: 'Recompense for what they used to do' [Surah al-Waqi'ah 56:24]. Since recompense occurs upon their actions, He is the Creator of their actions. If he says: Did not Allah, exalted, say: 'He said, Do you worship what you carve?' [Surah as-Saffat 37:95], meaning the idols which they carved? So what prevents you from thinking that His saying: 'created you and what you do' intended the idols which they made? It is said to him: What you thought is wrong, because the idols are carved by them in reality, but Allah's saying: 'Do you worship what you carve?' refers to them, and the wood is not made by them in reality, so His saying: 'created you and what you do' refers to them. If a speaker says: Did not Allah, exalted, say: 'It swallows what they fabricate' [Surah al-A'raf 7:117], and He did not intend their fabrication? So what prevents you from thinking that His saying: 'created you and what you do' does not refer to their actions? It is said to him: 'What they fabricate' are the ropes which they made to appear to the people as though they were moving snakes, and their fabrication is their making an illusion. So He intended by His saying 'they fabricate' i.e., they make people imagine that they are moving snakes, and their fabrication is their making something appear contrary to what it actually is. So the ropes are what they fabricate and make people imagine that they move in reality, and they are what the staff swallows. And it is not permissible that they actually make the wood, so it is not permissible that Allah, exalted, intended His saying 'created you and what you do' to refer to them, and it is necessary that it refers to actions, just as His saying 'Recompense for what they used to do' refers to actions. So if a claimant were to claim that Allah's saying: 'created you and what you do' ...
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two objections against the doctrine that human actions are created by Allah. The author, Imam Ash'ari, presents the objections and answers them sequentially. The first objection: The objector asks why they claim that human actions (aksab al-ibad) are created by Allah. The answer cites two Qur'anic verses: 'Allah created you and what you do' (37:96) and 'Recompense for what they used to do' (56:24). Since recompense (jaza') is based on actions, the Creator of those actions must be Allah. The objector then raises a second objection: Could the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' refer to the idols that the disbelievers carved, as in the verse 'Do you worship what you carve?' (37:95)? The answer distinguishes between the two verses: 'what you carve' refers to the idols, which are actually carved by humans, but 'what you do' in 37:96 cannot refer to idols because the idols are not 'made' by humans in reality—they are merely carved from pre-existing material. Thus, the verse must refer to their actions. A third objection is presented: In the verse about Prophet Moses' staff swallowing the magicians' ropes (7:117), the phrase 'what they fabricate' (ma ya'fikun) refers to the ropes, not the act of fabrication; so similarly, 'what you do' could refer to something other than actions. The answer explains that 'fabrication' (ifk) here means illusion or deception, not actual creation. The magicians made the ropes appear to be snakes through trickery, but they did not create the ropes; they only made people imagine they were snakes. Therefore, the verse still refers to an action (the act of making illusions), not an object. The passage concludes by stating that if it is not permissible for humans to actually create wood, then the verse cannot refer to the wood, but must refer to actions, consistent with the recompense verse. The text cuts off at the beginning of a new hypothetical objection.

Key Terms
إفك
تخييل
أعمال

What does the word 'إفك' (fabrication) mean in the context of the verse about the magicians in Surah al-A'raf?
A) Lies and false statements
B) Illusion or deception, making something appear other than it is
C) Real snakes that the magicians created
D) The staff of Moses

Key Takeaway
Imam Ash'ari shows that the word 'fabrication' in the Moses story refers to an act of deception, not the physical ropes, reinforcing that 'what you do' refers to actual actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you ever feel as though it is entirely your own creation, independent of Allah's will? How does this passage's insistence that actions are created by Allah challenge that feeling?
?
The magicians deceived others with illusions, but you might deceive yourself. In what area of your life are you believing an illusion—something that appears real but is actually false—regarding your own abilities or actions?
?
If the staff of Moses exposed the magicians' trick, what 'staff' in your life—a verse, a scholar, a trial—has exposed an illusion you believed? Are you willing to abandon that illusion now?

Ash'ari's Refutation: 'Khalaqakum wa ma ta'malun' Refers to Actions
Ash'ari refutes an objection by clarifying the magicians' verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ash'ari's argument that the verse 'He created you and what you do' necessarily refers to human actions, not to the physical objects they produce.

Core Idea
The verse 'what you do' refers to deeds, not artifacts.

This lesson examines a key objection raised by those who claim that 'what you do' in the Qur'an includes the objects themselves, like idols. Imam Ash'ari responds by analyzing a parallel verse about the magicians of Pharaoh, showing that the objects were not created by them; only the act of illusion-making was. This clarifies that divine creation encompasses human actions, not their material products.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the passage carefully. Notice how the objector uses the verse about the magicians to argue that 'ma ta'malun' could mean artifacts. Then see Ash'ari's point-by-point response.
2
Understand the magicians' illusion
Ash'ari explains that the magicians' 'fabrication' (ifk) was the illusion, not the ropes themselves. The ropes were pre-existing objects; the magicians only made them appear as snakes.
This distinction is crucial: the act of illusion is created, but the ropes are not.
3
Grasp the analogy with 'recompense'
Ash'ari draws a parallel with the verse 'recompense for what they used to do', which clearly refers to actions. If 'ma ta'malun' meant artifacts, then 'recompense for what they used to do' could also be twisted to mean recompense for artifacts, which is absurd.
4
See why the objection fails
The objector's analogy breaks down because the magicians did not create the ropes. So the verse 'He created you and what you do' must refer to the act of carving, not the carved idols.
This argument preserves the Islamic doctrine that Allah creates all actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل: أليس قد قال الله تعالى: {تَلْقَفُ مَا يَأْفِكُونَ} [الأعراف: 117]، ولم يُرِد إفكهم، فما أنكرت أن لا يرجع بقوله: {خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ} إلى أعمالهم؟ قيل له: الذي يَأْفِكُونَ هو الأمثلة التي خَيَّلُوا إلى الناس أنها حيَّات تسعى، وإفكهم تخييلهم؛ فأراد بقوله: {يَأْفِكُونَ} أي يُخَيِّلُونَ إلى الناس أنها حيَّات تسعى، وإفكهم هو إيهامهم الشيء على خلاف ما هو بسبيله؛ فالأمثلة هي التي يأفكون، ويخيلون إلى الناس أنها تسعى في الحقيقة، وهي التي تَلْقَفُها العصا. وليس يجوز أن يعملوا الخشب في الحقيقة، فلم يجز أن يكون الله تعالى أراد بقوله: {خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ} إليها، ووجب أن يرجع إلى الأعمال، كما رجع بقوله: {جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ} إلى الأعمال. فلو جاز لزاعم أن يزعم أن قول الله تعالى: {خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ} أراد به غير أعمالهم كما أراد بقوله: {وَمَا يَأْفِكُونَ} غير إفكهم، لساغ لزاعم أن يزعم أن قول الله تعالى: {جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ} إنما أراد به غير أعمالهم كما أراد بقوله: {خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ} غير أعمالهم، كما أن قوله: {وَمَا يَأْفِكُونَ} إنما أراد به إفكهم، فلما لم يجز هذا، لم يجز ما قاله هذا.
If someone says: 'Did not Allah Most High say: "It swallows what they fabricate" (7:117), and He did not intend their fabrication? So why do you deny that His saying "He created you and what you do" (37:96) does not refer to their actions?' It is said to him: 'That which they fabricate (ya'fikun) are the ropes that they made people imagine were live snakes, and their fabrication (ifk) is their making illusions; so He intended by His saying "they fabricate" i.e., they make people imagine that they are live snakes, and their fabrication is their causing people to imagine something contrary to what it is. So the ropes are what they fabricate and imagine to people that they are actually moving, and they are what the staff swallows. And it is not permissible that they actually make wood (work wood) in reality, so it is not permissible that Allah Most High intended by His saying "He created you and what you do" to refer to them (the wood), and it is necessary that it refers to actions, just as His saying "recompense for what they used to do" (6:146) refers to actions. So if it were permissible for a claimant to claim that the saying of Allah Most High "He created you and what you do" intended other than their actions, just as He intended by His saying "and what they fabricate" other than their fabrication, then it would be permissible for a claimant to claim that the saying of Allah Most High "recompense for what they used to do" only intended other than their actions, just as He intended by His saying "He created you and what you do" other than their actions, while His saying "and what they fabricate" only intended their fabrication. So when this is not permissible, what this (objector) said is not permissible.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer form of argument. The objector cites the verse "It swallows what they fabricate" (7:117) from the story of Moses and the magicians, arguing that the word "what they fabricate" (ma ya'fikun) refers to the physical ropes they cast, not to the act of fabrication itself. He then analogizes: if in that verse "ma" refers to the product (the ropes), then in the verse "He created you and what you do" (37:96), "what you do" (ma ta'malun) could also refer to the product (the carved idols) rather than to the act of carving. Ash'ari answers by first clarifying that "what they fabricate" (ya'fikun) actually means the ropes themselves, but the act of fabrication (ifk) is the illusion they created. The ropes are the objects that received the act of illusion-making. The staff swallows those objects. Then he states that it is impossible for the magicians to actually create the wood (i.e., bring it into existence); they only worked on pre-existing wood. Therefore, Allah's saying "He created you and what you do" cannot refer to the wood as a product, because that would imply they create the wood. It must refer to their actions (the acts of carving). He then supports this by noting that the phrase "recompense for what they used to do" (6:146) clearly refers to actions, not products. If one were to claim that "He created you and what you do" refers to non-actions (products), then by analogy one could claim that "recompense for what they used to do" also refers to non-actions, which is absurd. Thus the objection fails.

إفك
أمثلة

أعمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think the phrase 'ma ta'malun' in verse 37:96 includes the physical objects (idols) that people make.
Correction: Ash'ari demonstrates that it refers to the actions themselves, because the magicians did not create the wood (ropes) they used; they only made an illusion. Thus, Allah's creation of 'what you do' is the act, not the artifact.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason Ash'ari gives that 'Khalaqakum wa ma ta'malun' must refer to actions rather than artifacts?
A) Because the objector's analogy is invalid.
B) Because the magicians did not actually create the wood, only worked on it.
C) Because the word 'ma' always refers to actions in the Qur'an.
D) Because the staff swallowed the ropes, not the actions.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari proves that 'He created you and what you do' refers to human actions by showing that the magicians created only the illusion, not the physical ropes, thus the verse cannot refer to artifacts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'He created you and what you do,' do you truly believe that every action of yours is created by Allah? How does that change your feeling of pride in your good deeds or guilt in your sins? Will you begin each day by acknowledging that your very ability to act is a gift from Him?
?
Ash'ari meticulously defends the clear meaning of the Quran against someone who twists it. Is there an area of your life where you have twisted Allah's words to justify your own desires? What would it cost you to submit to the plain meaning of the text today?
?
The magicians created an illusion that looked real. How many of your 'good deeds' are illusions—done for show or out of habit—while your heart is far from Allah? Will you ask Allah to show you the reality of your actions and to purify your intentions before you perform the next one?

Proof from Analogy: Actions Created by Allah
Ash'ari presents a logical proof from analogy that human actions are created by Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses a logical analogy (qiyas) to prove that human actions, including their moral qualities, are created by Allah.

Core Idea
The qualities of actions are beyond human control, proving they must be created by a Maker.

Before we dive into the source passage, consider this: How can we know that our actions are not entirely our own? Ash'ari presents a powerful argument from analogy. He observes that both disbelief and faith have fixed qualities that human effort cannot change. From this, he builds a logical proof that every action, with its specific nature, must be created by Allah. The passage is concise but packed with reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two observations
Read the passage and notice what Ash'ari observes about disbelief (kufr) and faith (iman). Disbelief is ugly, corrupt, false, contradictory; faith is good, wearisome, painful.
These qualities are fixed, not subject to human desire.
2
Note the failure of human will
Ash'ari points out that the disbeliever tries to make disbelief good but fails, and the believer cannot make faith free from pain and weariness. This shows that the qualities are beyond human control.
3
Grasp the general principle
He then states a general rule: an action does not occur in its true nature except from a maker (muhdith) who brings it into existence in that state.
This principle forms the core of the analogy.
4
Follow the conditional argument
Ash'ari uses a reductio ad absurdum: if an action could occur in its true nature without a maker, then anything could become an action without a maker, which is impossible. Therefore, actions must have a maker.
This reasoning proves that Allah creates actions with their specific qualities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل من القياس، على خلق أعمال الناس: أنا وجدنا الكفر قبيحا فاسدا باطلا متناقضا خلافا لمن خالف. ووجدنا الإيمان حسنا متعبا مؤلما. ووجدنا الكافر يقصد ويجهد نفسه، إلى أن يكون الكفر حسنا حقا، فيكون بخلاف قصده، ووجدنا الإيمان، لو شاء المؤمن أن لا يكون متعبا مؤلما ولا مَرْمِضًا، لم يكن ذلك كائنا على حسب مشيئته وإرادته. وقد علمنا أن الفعل لا يحدث على حقيقته، إلا من محدث أحدثه عليها؛ لأنه لو جاز أن يحدث، على حقيقته، لا من محدث أحدثه على ما هو عليه؛ لجاز أن يحدث الشيء فعلا لا من محدث أحدثه فعلا: فلما لم يجز ذلك، صح أنه لم يحدث على حقيقته، إلا من محدث أحدثه عليها.
And the proof from analogy (qiyās) on the creation of people's actions: we found disbelief (kufr) to be ugly (qabīḥ), corrupt, false, contradictory, opposite to those who oppose. And we found faith (īmān) to be good (ḥasan), wearisome, painful. And we found the disbeliever intends and exerts himself so that disbelief would be good and true, but it turns out contrary to his intention. And we found faith: if the believer wished that it not be wearisome, painful, nor grievous, that would not happen according to his will and desire. And we know that an action does not occur in its true nature except from a maker (muḥdith) who brings it into existence in that state; because if it were permissible for it to occur in its true nature without a maker who brings it into existence as it is, then it would be permissible for a thing to become an action without a maker who makes it an action. So when that is not permissible, it is correct that it does not occur in its true nature except from a maker who brings it into existence in that state.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage is a proof from analogy (qiyas) demonstrating that human actions are created by Allah. Ash'ari begins by observing two facts about moral qualities: disbelief (kufr) is ugly (qabih) and painful, while faith (iman) is good (hasan) yet also wearisome and painful. He then notes that the disbeliever tries to make kufr appear good but fails—it remains ugly. Similarly, if a believer wishes his faith to be free from weariness and pain, it does not happen according to his wish. This shows that the qualities (husn, qubh) and the painfulness of actions are not subject to human desire or effort. Next, he states a general principle: a physical action cannot occur in its true nature (i.e., with its specific qualities) except from a maker (muhdith) who brings it into existence with those qualities. He supports this with a conditional argument: if it were possible for an action to occur in its true nature without a maker, then it would be possible for a thing to become an action without any maker at all, which is impossible. Therefore, it is necessary that every action occurs in its true nature only from a maker who creates it with those qualities. This implies that the particular qualities (goodness, ugliness, pain) of actions must also be created by a maker—Allah. Thus human actions, including their moral qualities, are created by Allah.

Key Terms

كفر
إيمان
حسن
قبيح
محدث
فعل
حقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the moral and experiential qualities of actions (e.g., painfulness, goodness) are determined by human intention alone.
Correction: Ash'ari shows that these qualities are fixed and beyond human control. The disbeliever cannot make disbelief good, and the believer cannot make faith painless. Therefore, these qualities must be created by Allah, not by human will.

Checkpoint
What is the key logical principle Ash'ari uses to prove that actions must have a maker?
A) If an action could occur without a maker, then anything could become an action without a maker.
B) The disbeliever's failure to make kufr good proves there is no creator.
C) Actions are caused by human free will alone.
D) Good actions require a good maker, but bad actions do not.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari's proof from analogy shows that because the moral and experiential qualities of actions are fixed and beyond human will, they must be created by Allah, not by us.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience difficulty, pain, or weariness in your faith, do you silently resent Allah or do you recognize that He created those very qualities in your action for a purpose? What does this lesson demand you to admit about your lack of control over the nature of your own deeds?
?
You think you own your actions—but can you change the moral quality of a sin you committed? Can you make a forbidden act good by your intention alone? This passage says the disbeliever tried and failed. What does that say about your sense of spiritual independence? Are you ready to surrender the illusion that you are the source of your actions' value?
?
If every aspect of your action—even its painfulness or ugliness—is created by Allah, whom do you blame when you find your worship burdensome? Do you dare to hold yourself accountable, knowing that the burden itself is from Him? What commitment will you make today to accept the qualities Allah chooses for your deeds?

Scriptural Proof That Actions Are Created by God
Al-Ash'ari argues from Quranic consistency that actions are created by God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses Quranic consistency to prove that human actions are created by God.

Core Idea
The Quran consistently refers to actions as created, so reinterpreting one verse breaks the pattern.

Imam al-Ash'ari now turns to the Quran to ground his theological position. He shows that interpreting the verse 'He created you and what you do' as referring to something other than the actions would force an absurd interpretation of other verses. This argument from consistency is a powerful tool in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the argument's flow come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with a heading stating the position.
2
Identify the opponent's re-interpretation
Al-Ash'ari addresses someone who claims the verse 'He created you and what you do' refers to things other than actions. Try to see why someone might think that.
3
Trace the logical implication
If you allow that re-interpretation, then the same principle must apply to other verses like 'Recompense for what they used to do'. Ask: would that make sense?
This is the core of the reductio ad absurdum.
4
Conclude with consistency
Since the implication is absurd, the only consistent reading is that actions themselves are meant. Therefore, actions are created by God.
This shows the power of scriptural consistency in theological argument.

أَفْعَالُ العِبادِ مِن خَلْقِ الله تَعْمَلُونَ أرادَ غير أعمالهم كما أراد بقوله: ﴿وَمَا يَأْفِكُونَ﴾ غير إفكهم، لَساغَ لِزاعِمٍ أن يَزْعُمَ أنَّ قولَ اللَّهِ -تعالى-: ﴿جَزَاء بِمَا كَانُوا يَعْمَلُونَ﴾ إنَّما أراد به غير أعمالهم كما أراد بقوله: خَلَقَكُمْ وَمَا تَعْمَلُونَ غير أعمالهم، كما أن قوله: ﴿وَمَا يَأْفِكُونَ﴾ إنَّما أراد به إفكهم، فلمَّا لَمْ يَجُزْ هَذَا، لم يجز ما قالَهُ هَذَا
The actions of servants are from the creation of God. 'You do' He intended other than their actions, just as He intended in His saying: 'And they fabricate not' other than their fabrication, it would be permissible for a claimant to claim that God's saying - exalted be He - 'Recompense for what they used to do' only intended other than their actions, just as He intended in His saying 'He created you and what you do' other than their actions, just as His saying 'And they fabricate not' only intended their fabrication. So when this is not permissible, what this one said is not permissible.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage presents a scriptural proof that human actions are created by God. It begins with the heading 'The actions of servants are from the creation of God.' The argument proceeds by pointing out an inconsistency in the interpretation of certain Quranic verses. If someone claims that the verse 'He created you and what you do' means something other than the actions themselves, then by the same logic, the verse 'Recompense for what they used to do' would also have to mean something other than their actions, which is absurd. Similarly, the verse 'And they fabricate not' clearly refers to their fabrication. Therefore, unless the opponent is willing to interpret all similar verses inconsistently, he must accept that 'He created you and what you do' refers to the actions themselves. Thus the actions are created by God.

Key Terms
أفعال العباد
خلق الله
تأويل
آيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the verse 'خلقكم وما تعملون' could mean God created them and their tools, not their actions.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that this interpretation would force an inconsistent reading of other verses, so the only consistent reading is that actions are created.

Checkpoint
What is the logical consequence if someone interprets 'خلقكم وما تعملون' as meaning something other than their actions?
A) It would make all verses about actions metaphorical.
B) They would have to interpret 'جزاء بما كانوا يعملون' as also meaning other than their actions, which is absurd.
C) They would be guilty of disbelief.
D) The verse would become unintelligible.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari employs a reductio ad absurdum argument to show that the Quranic verse 'He created you and what you do' must be understood as referring to actions themselves, affirming that God creates human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If Allah creates every action you do, including your sins, how does this affect the way you seek forgiveness? Do you rely on His mercy alone, or do you feel entitled because 'you' stopped sinning?
?
The verse 'He created you and what you do' leaves no room for attributing any action to yourself. Are there areas of your life where you still think you are in control? Surrender them to Allah right now.

Al-Ash'ari's Rational Proof for Divine Creation of Actions
Al-Ash'ari uses analogical reasoning to prove actions require a creator distinct from the human agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Ash'ari's analogical argument that human actions, including their moral qualities, are created by God and not by the human agent.

Core Idea
Actions and their qualities require an external intender, not the agent.

Al-Ash'ari presents a rational proof from analogy to establish that God creates all human actions. He observes that the actual qualities of actions (faith as tiring, disbelief as false) are contrary to the agent's desires, showing that the agent is not the efficient cause. He then argues that every action in its true nature must come from an efficient cause that intends it, which for disbelief and faith cannot be the human agent.

Guided Path
1
Observe the data
Read the first part of the passage where Al-Ash'ari notes that faith is good but tiring and painful, and that the disbeliever wants disbelief to be good but it turns out bad. This shows a disconnect between intention and outcome.
This observation is the starting point of the proof.
2
Understand the causal principle
Al-Ash'ari lays out a general principle: an action cannot occur in its true nature (حقيقته) without an efficient cause (محدث) that intends it. He argues by contradiction: if it could, then all actions could lack a cause, which is absurd.
The principle is key to the argument.
3
Apply the principle to disbelief and faith
Since disbelief occurs as bad and false, but the disbeliever desires it to be good, the efficient cause cannot be the disbeliever. Similarly, faith occurs as tiring and painful, but the believer cannot change that. Therefore, the efficient cause must be God.
This yields the conclusion that God creates all actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليلُ مِن القِياسِ، عَلَى خلقِ أعمالِ النَّاسِ : أَنَّا وَجَدْنَا الإيمان حسنًا مُتعبًا مؤلما . ووجَدْنا الكافِرَ يقصِدُ ويُجهد نفسه، إلَى أنْ يكونَ الكُفرُ حسنًا حقًا، فيكُونُ بخلافِ قصْدِه، ووجَدْنا الإيمان، لو شاءَ المؤمنُ أن لا يكونَ مُتعِبًا مؤلِمًا ولا مُرْمِضًا ، لَمْ يكُنْ ذلك كائنا عَلَى حَسَبِ مَشِيئَتِهِ وإرادتِهِ . وقد علمنا أنَّ الفِعلَ لا يحدثُ على حقيقتِهِ، إِلا مِنْ مُحدِثٍ أحدَثَهُ عليها ؛ لأنه لو جاز أنْ يَحدُثَ، على حقيقتِه، لَا مِنْ مُحدِثٍ أَحدَثَه على ما هُوَ عليه ؛ لجاز أن يحدثَ الشيء فعلا لا مِنْ مُحدِث أحْدَثَه فعلا : فلما لم يجُز ذلكَ ، صح أنهُ لمْ يحدث على حقيقتِهِ ، إِلَّا من مُحدِث أَحْدَثَه على ما هو عليه، وهو قاصد إلى ذلك ؛ لأنَّه لو جاز حدوثُ فِعل، على الحقيقة، لا مِنْ قاصدِ، لَمْ يُوْمَنْ أن تكونَ الأفعالُ كلُّهَا كذلك، كما أنَّه لو جازَ حدوث فعل لا مِنْ فاعِل لم يُؤْمَنْ أن تكون الأفعالُ كلُّها كذلِكَ . وإذا كان هذا هكذا ، فقد وجب أن يكونَ لِلْكُفْرِ مُحدِثٌ أحدثَهُ كُفرًا باطلا قبيحًا، وهو قاصد إلى ذلك، ولَنْ يجوز أن يكونَ المُحدِثُ لَهُ هُوَ الكافِرَ ، الذي يُرِيدُ أن يكونَ الكُفْرُ حَسَنًا صَوابًا حقًّا ، فيكون على خِلافِ ذلك . وكذلك للإيمان محدِثٌ أحدَثَه، على حقيقته متعباً مؤلماً مُرْمِضًا ، غيرُ المؤمن الذي لو جَهِدَ أن يقع الإيمانُ خلاف ما وقع، مِنْ إيلامِهِ وإتعابه وإرماضه، لم يكنْ لَهُ إلى ذلِكَ سَبِيلٌ .
And the proof from analogy for the creation of people's actions: we found faith to be good, tiring, painful. And we found the disbeliever intends and exerts himself so that disbelief becomes good and true, but it turns out contrary to his intention. And we found faith, if the believer wished that it not be tiring, painful, or distressing, that would not happen according to his wish and will. And we know that an action only occurs in its true nature from an efficient cause that brings it into existence upon it; because if it were permissible for it to occur in its true nature without an efficient cause that brings it into existence as it actually is, then it would be permissible for a thing to occur as an action without any efficient cause that makes it an action. So since that is not permissible, it is correct that it only occurs in its true nature from an efficient cause that brings it into existence as it actually is, and that cause is intending that; because if the occurrence of an action in its true nature without an intender were permissible, it could not be safe that all actions are like that, just as if the occurrence of an action without a doer were permissible, it could not be safe that all actions are like that. And if this is so, then disbelief must have an efficient cause that brings it into existence as disbelief, false, ugly, and that cause intends that, and it is not permissible that the efficient cause for it be the disbeliever himself, who wants disbelief to be good, correct, true, so it is opposite to that. And similarly, faith has an efficient cause that brings it into existence in its true nature as tiring, painful, distressing, other than the believer, who if he strove to make faith occur contrary to what it did occur, from its pain, tiredness, and distress, he would have no way to that.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage provides a rational proof (analogical reasoning) that human actions are created by God. The author begins by observing two facts: (1) Faith is actually good but also tiring and painful. (2) The disbeliever exerts himself to make disbelief good and true, but it turns out to be opposite (i.e., bad and false). Similarly, the believer cannot prevent faith from being tiring and painful even if he wishes. This shows that the actual quality of actions is not under the agent's control. The author then lays down a principle: an action only occurs in its actual nature (حقيقته) from an efficient cause (محدث) that brings it into existence exactly as it is, with intention (قاصد). If it could occur without such a cause, then all actions could lack a cause, which is absurd. Applying this to disbelief and faith: disbelief occurs as false and ugly, but the disbeliever desires it to be good and true. Therefore, the efficient cause cannot be the disbeliever; it must be an external intender, namely God. Similarly, faith occurs as tiring and painful, but the believer cannot change that, so its efficient cause is God, not the believer. Thus, God creates all actions, including their specific qualities.

Key Terms

قياس
محدث
قاصد
فعل
كفر
إيمان
حقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the moral agent determines the moral quality of his own action.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that the quality (kufr as bad, iman as good but painful) is objectively fixed and not up to the agent; thus the agent cannot be the efficient cause.

Checkpoint
What principle does Al-Ash'ari establish about the occurrence of an action in its true nature?
A) It can occur without any cause.
B) It must occur from an efficient cause that intends it.
C) It is always the result of the agent's intention.
D) It is determined by the action's intrinsic nature alone.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari proves that God is the creator of all human actions because the qualities of actions do not align with the agent's intentions, necessitating an external efficient cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform an action that you intend to be good but it brings pain or difficulty, do you recognize that your will alone cannot control its outcome? How does this realization shape your reliance on Allah in your daily actions?
?
This lesson shows that even the disbeliever cannot make his disbelief good in reality. Reflect on your own intentions: are there areas in your life where you try to define good and evil based on your desires, ignoring the reality set by your Creator? What would it take to surrender that?
?
Al-Ash'ari proves that the qualities of actions are fixed by an external intender. Consider a sin you have committed: did you truly intend it to be harmful or ugly? How does the knowledge that Allah creates its true nature affect your repentance and gratitude for His mercy?

Objections on Kasb and Divine Agency
Al-Ash'ari answers objections about kasb's implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Ash'ari defends the doctrine that only Allah is the true doer and inventor of acts, while humans acquire them.

Core Idea
Kasb affirms divine agency, not human independence.

Having defined kasb, Al-Ash'ari now faces objections that challenge its consistency. If an act is acquired, why doesn't it imply multiple agents? The responses clarify that divine attributes of creation and capability remain exclusive to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once to follow the objection-response structure.
Notice the parallel structure of the two objections.
2
Identify the two objections
The objector first argues about 'doer', then about 'capable'. Note how each answer builds on the previous.
3
Analyze the answers
The first answer is terse ('thus we say'), the second expands on the meaning of capability and invention. Both affirm exclusive divine agency.
The second answer uses the term 'ikhtirāʿ' (invention).
4
Reflect on the doctrine
Consider how this refutes any notion of human partnership in creation. Kasb is not a middle ground but a reaffirmation of tawḥīd.
This connects to the broader Ash'ari stance on qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : فلم لا دلَّ وقوع الفعل، الذي هو كَسْبٌ ، على أَنَّهُ لا فاعلَ لَهُ إِلَّا الله ، كما دلَّ على أنَّه لا خالق إِلَّا اللَّه -تعالى؟ قيل له : كذلك نقول . فإن قالَ : فلِمَ لا دل على أنه لا قادِرَ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا الله -عز وجل-؟ قيل له : لا فاعل لهُ علَى حقيقتِه إِلَّا اللَّهُ -تعالى-، ولا قادر عليهِ أن يكون على ما هُوَ عليْهِ ، من حقيقتِهِ ، أَنْ يَخْتَرِعَهُ) ، إِلَّا اللَّهُ -تعالى-.
If someone says: Why does not the occurrence of the action, which is kasb (acquisition), indicate that there is no doer of it except Allah, just as it indicates that there is no creator except Allah - exalted? It is said to him: Thus we say. If he says: Why does it not indicate that there is no one capable of it except Allah - mighty and majestic? It is said to him: There is no doer of it in its reality except Allah - exalted - and no one capable of it to be as it is, in its reality, that He invents it, except Allah - exalted.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents two objections regarding the concept of kasb (acquisition) and Al-Ash'ari's responses. First objection: If an action is described as kasb, why does it not show that there is no doer but Allah, just as it shows there is no creator but Allah? The answer is simply: 'Thus we say'—meaning that kasb indeed implies that Allah is the sole doer (fāʿil) of the act in its reality. Second objection: Why does kasb not indicate that there is no one capable (qādir) of it except Allah? The answer clarifies: in its true reality, there is no doer except Allah, and no one is capable of making it as it is, including the act of inventing (ikhtirāʿ) it, except Allah. This reinforces the Ash'ari position that human actions are created by Allah, while humans acquire them; the term 'kasb' does not imply independent agency.

Key Terms
كسب (kasb/acquisition)
فاعل (doer)
خالق (creator)
قادر (capable)
اختراع (invention)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'kasb' implies that humans share in creation or have independent capability.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari states that in reality only Allah is the doer and the one capable of inventing the act.

Checkpoint
How does Al-Ash'ari answer the objection that kasb indicates no one is capable of the act except Allah?
A) He says 'Thus we say' and moves on.
B) He explains that in reality only Allah is the doer and the one capable of inventing the act.
C) He denies that kasb has any relation to capability.
D) He argues that humans have partial capability.

Key Takeaway
Kasb does not compromise divine exclusivity; only Allah is the true doer and the one capable of inventing actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you feel overwhelmed by your own failures, do you truly believe that only Allah has the power to change your state? What would it mean to rely on that belief right now?
?
If you really accept that you cannot invent any action from nothing, what would you stop taking credit for today, and to whom would you redirect your gratitude?

Allah Creates All Human Actions
Al-Ash'ari proves that Allah is the true creator of all actions, including human acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's argument that Allah alone is the true creator of all human actions, and how the concept of 'acquisition' (kasb) does not imply human independence.

Core Idea
Allah creates all actions; humans merely acquire them without being true creators.

This passage from al-Ash'ari's al-Luma' tackles one of the most debated issues in Islamic theology: who creates human actions? Using logical reasoning, al-Ash'ari demonstrates that since neither the human nor any body can be the true originator of an action, Allah must be. He then addresses objections related to the term 'acquisition' (kasb), clarifying that while humans acquire actions, the true creative act remains with Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the dialectical style with objections and answers.
The passage uses technical terms like muḥdith, fāʿil, muktasib.
2
Identify the main argument
Find the conditional premise: if the servant cannot be the true originator of faith/disbelief, then Allah must be. Note the reasoning about bodies not acting on other bodies.
3
Examine the three objections
The opponent raises three points about why kasb does not prove Allah as sole doer, sole power, sole acquirer. Trace Al-Ash'ari's responses.
The third objection gets the most detailed reply.
4
Understand the analogy of involuntary motion
Al-Ash'ari gives the example of a trembling hand: Allah causes the motion, but the hand is not the true doer. Relate this to acquisition.
This analogy clarifies the distinction between true doer and apparent actor.
5
Reflect on the key distinction
Actions necessarily have a true doer, but not necessarily a true acquirer. Realize that 'acquisition' is a metaphorical attribution to humans, while Allah is the real creator.
This guards against the misconception that humans create their own actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَفْعَالُ العِبادِ مِن خَلْقِ الله
وإذا لم يجز أن يكونَ المحدِثُ للكفر - على حقيقتِهِ - الكافر، وَلَا المحدِثُ للإيمانِ على حقيقته المؤمِنَ، فَقَدْ وَجَبَ أن يكونَ مُحدِثُ ذلك هُوَ اللَّهَ - تعالى - ربَّ العالمينَ، القاصِدَ إلى ذلِكَ ؛ لأنه لا يجوز أن يكونَ أحدَثَ ذلك جسمٌ مِنَ الأجْسامِ؛ لأنَّ الأجسام لا يجوزُ أن تفعل في غيرها شيئًا.
فإن قال قائل : فلم لا دلَّ وقوع الفعل، الذي هو كَسْبٌ ، على أَنَّهُ لا فاعلَ لَهُ إِلَّا الله ، كما دلَّ على أنَّه لا خالق إِلَّا اللَّهُ -تعالى؟ قيل له : كذلك نقول .
فإن قالَ : فلِمَ لا دل على أنه لا قادِرَ عَلَيْهِ إِلَّا الله -عز وجل-؟ قيل له : لا فاعل لهُ علَى حقيقتِه إِلَّا اللَّهُ -تعالى-، ولا قادر عليهِ أن يكون على ما هُوَ عليْهِ ، من حقيقتِهِ ، أَنْ يَخْتَرِعَهُ، إِلَّا اللَّهُ -تعالى-. فإن قالَ : فلِمَ لا دلَّ كونُهُ كَسْبًا على حقيقتِهِ، عَلَى أَنَّهُ لا مُكْتَسِبَ له في الحقيقةِ إِلَّا اللَّهُ؟
قِيلَ لَهُ: الأفعالُ لا بد لها من فاعل على حقيقتها ؛ لأنَّ الفعل لا يستَغْنِي عن فاعل، فإذا لم يكن فاعله على حقيقته الجسم، وجب أن يكونَ الله - تعالى - هو الفاعلَ لَهُ على حقيقته . وليس لا بدَّ للفعل من مكتسب يكتسبه على حقيقته ، كما لا بدَّ من فاعل يفعله على حقيقته ، فيجب إذا كانَ الفعلُ كَسْبا ؛ كانَ اللهُ -تعالى- هو المكتسب له على حقيقته .
ألا ترى أنَّ على أنَّ اللهَ -تعالى- هو حركة الاضطرارِ ـ الفاعل لها على حقيقتها ولا تدلُّ على أن المتحرك بها، في الحقيقة، هو الله - تعالى - ؛ إذْ كانت حركةً، كما كان هو الفاعل لها في الحقيقة؟
ولا يجب أن يكون المتحرك المضطر إليها فاعلا لها على حقيقتها ؛ إذ كان متحركًا بها على الحقيقة؛ إذْ كَانَ معنَى المُتحرِّكِ أنَّ الحركةَ حَلَّتْه ، ولم يكن ذلك جائزا على ربنا -تعالى-. وكذلك إذا كان الكَسْبُ دالا على فاعل فَعَلَه على حقيقته، لم يجب أن يدلَّ على أنَّ الفاعل له على حقيقته، هو المكتسب له، ولا على أنَّ المكتسب له على الحقيقة هو الفاعل له.
[Heading] The acts of servants are from the creation of Allah.
And if it is not permissible that the originator (al-muḥdith) of disbelief – in its true reality – be the disbeliever, nor that the originator of faith in its true reality be the believer, then it becomes necessary that the originator of that is Allah – exalted – the Lord of the worlds, the one intending that; because it is not permissible that a body among bodies originated that; because bodies are not permitted to do anything in other than themselves.
If someone says: Why does the occurrence of the action, which is acquisition (kasb), not indicate that there is no doer (fāʿil) of it except Allah, just as it indicates that there is no creator (khāliq) except Allah – exalted? It is said to him: Thus we say.
If he says: Why does it not indicate that there is no power over it except Allah – mighty and majestic? It is said to him: There is no doer of it in its true reality except Allah – exalted – and no one has power over it to be as it is, in its true reality, to originate it, except Allah – exalted. Then if he says: Why does its being acquisition in its true reality not indicate that there is no acquirer (muktasib) of it in reality except Allah? It is said to him: Actions necessarily have a doer in their true reality, because the action does not dispense with a doer. So if its doer in its true reality is not a body, then it is necessary that Allah – exalted – is its doer in its true reality. And it is not necessary for the action to have an acquirer who acquires it in its true reality, just as it is necessary to have a doer who does it in its true reality. Thus it is necessary that when the action is acquisition, Allah – exalted – is the acquirer of it in its true reality.
Do you not see that [the phrase may be garbled] Allah – exalted – is [the doer] of involuntary motion – the doer of it in its true reality – and it does not indicate that the one moved by it, in reality, is Allah – exalted – since it is a motion, just as He is the doer of it in reality? And it is not necessary that the one moved involuntarily to it be a doer of it in its true reality, since he is moved by it in reality; because the meaning of 'the moved' is that motion has settled in him, and that is not permissible for our Lord – exalted. And similarly, when acquisition indicates a doer who did it in its true reality, it is not necessary that it indicates that the doer of it in its true reality is the acquirer of it, nor that the acquirer of it in reality is the doer of it.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a proof that Allah is the true creator of all human actions, including acts of faith and disbelief, followed by objections and answers about the concept of acquisition (kasb). The argument begins by establishing that if the servant cannot be the true originator (muḥdith) of disbelief or faith – because that would entail impossible consequences – then the true originator must be Allah. This is reinforced by the claim that no body can originate an act in another body. The opponent then raises objections: why does the fact that an action is 'acquisition' not indicate that Allah is the sole doer just as it indicates He is the sole creator? Al-Ash'ari replies that he agrees – Allah is the sole true doer. The opponent then asks why kasb does not prove that Allah is the sole power over the action, and the answer is that Allah alone has true power and originates it. The third objection asks why kasb does not prove that Allah is the sole acquirer (muktasib). The answer is more detailed: actions necessarily have a true doer, but they do not necessarily have a true acquirer. If the doer is not a body, it must be Allah. Then, when the action is acquisition, Allah is the true acquirer – not the human. Al-Ash'ari provides an analogy: involuntary motion (like trembling) is done by Allah as its true doer, but that does not mean the moving body is the true doer. Similarly, the fact that an action is acquired by a human does not mean the human is the true doer; the true doer (and acquirer) is Allah. The passage guards against the misunderstanding that human 'acquisition' makes the human an independent creator.

Key Terms
أَفْعَال العباد
كسب
مكتسب
فاعل
محدث
حركة الاضطرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because an action is 'acquired' by a human, the human is the true originator of that action.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari clarifies that acquisition does not make the human a true doer; the true doer and acquirer is Allah, as shown by the analogy of involuntary motion.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari, why must Allah be the true doer of all actions, including human acts of disbelief and faith?
A) Because actions have no real doer other than Allah.
B) Because if a servant were the true doer of disbelief, it would be impossible; and bodies cannot create actions in others.
C) Because humans are only capable of acquisition, not creation, but Allah could delegate creation.
D) Because the human will is not free, so Allah forces actions upon them.

Key Takeaway
Allah is the true creator of all actions; human acquisition is a metaphorical attribution, not independent creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Can you point to a specific sin you commit repeatedly and honestly ask yourself: 'Am I excusing myself because Allah created it?'
?
The passage uses the example of involuntary motion to show that the one moved is not the doer. When you perform a good deed, do you secretly feel you deserve credit? How would your prayer (ṣalāh) change if you reminded yourself before every posture that Allah is the true mover?
?
Al-Ash'ari argues that neither the believer nor the disbeliever is the true originator of their faith or disbelief. If you have been blessed with īmān, does this make you grateful or proud? What would it cost you to attribute your īmān entirely to Allah's creation and not to your own effort?

Every Action Requires an Agent
Al-Ash'ari argues actions need an agent; God is that agent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why every action necessarily has a true agent, and if that agent is not a physical body, it must be God.

Core Idea
Actions cannot exist without an agent; God is the ultimate agent of all acts.

This passage establishes a foundational principle of Ash'ari theology: every action requires a real agent. Imam al-Ash'ari argues that if the apparent agent (like a human body) is not the true agent, then God must be. This sets the stage for the doctrine of kasb.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening argument
Read the first part of the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the strong claim: an action cannot do without an agent (fā'il) in reality.
The term 'fā'il' means the one who truly brings about the action.
2
Identify the syllogism
The argument is a simple conditional: if the agent is not a body, then it must be God. Trace the logic: actions need an agent; if that agent is not the body we see, then God is the agent.
3
Connect to kasb
Al-Ash'ari then applies this to acquisition (kasb): even if an action is called kasb, its true agent is God, not the human.
The term 'muktasib' (acquirer) will be explained in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيل له: الأفعال لا بد لها من فاعل على حقيقتها؛ لأن الفعل لا يستغني عن فاعل، فإذا لم يكن فاعله على حقيقته الجسم، وجب أن يكون الله تعالى هو الفاعل له على حقيقته. وليس لا بد للفعل من مكتسب يكتسبه على حقيقته، كما لا بد من فاعل يفعله على حقيقته، فيجب إذا كان الفعل كسبا؛ كان الله تعالى هو المكتسب له على حقيقته. ألا ترى أن الحركة الاضطرارية إنما دلت على أن الله تعالى هو الفاعل لها على حقيقتها ولا تدل على أن المتحرك بها، في الحقيقة، هو الله تعالى؛ إذ كانت حركة، كما كان هو الفاعل لها في الحقيقة؟ ولا يجب أن يكون المتحرك المضطر إليها فاعلا لها على حقيقتها؛ إذ كان متحركا بها على الحقيقة؛ إذ كان معنى المتحرك أن الحركة حلته، ولم يكن ذلك جائزا على ربنا تعالى. وكذلك إذا كان الكسب دالا على فاعل فعله على حقيقته، لم يجب أن يدل على أن الفاعل له على حقيقته، هو المكتسب له، ولا على أن المكتسب له على الحقيقة هو الفاعل له، على حقيقته؛ إذ كان المكتسب مكتسبا للشيء؛ لأنه وقع بقدرة له عليه محدثة، ولم يجز أن يكون رب العالمين قادرا على الشيء بقدرة محدثة، فلم يجز أن يكون مكتسبا للكسب، وإن كان فاعلا له في الحقيقة.
It was said to him: Actions necessarily have an agent in reality, because the action cannot do without an agent. If its agent is not in reality the body, then it is necessary that God Almighty is the agent of it in reality. And it is not necessary that the action have an acquirer who acquires it in reality, just as it is necessary that it have an agent who does it in reality. So if the action is acquisition, then God Almighty is the acquirer of it in reality. Do you not see that the involuntary movement indicates that God Almighty is the agent of it in reality, and it does not indicate that the one moving by it, in reality, is God Almighty, since it is a movement, just as He is the agent of it in reality? And it is not necessary that the one compelled to it be an agent of it in reality, since he is moving by it in reality, because the meaning of 'the moving' is that movement has occurred in him, and that is not permissible for our Lord Almighty. And likewise, if acquisition indicates an agent who did it in reality, it is not necessary that it indicate that the agent of it in reality is the acquirer of it, nor that the acquirer of it in reality is the agent of it in reality, since the acquirer acquires the thing because it occurs by a power he possesses that is originated, and it is not permissible that the Lord of the worlds be powerful over a thing by an originated power, so it is not permissible that He be an acquirer of the acquisition, even if He is an agent of it in reality.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a proof establishing that God is the true agent (fā'il) of all actions, including the acquisition (kasb) attributed to humans. The author begins by stating a premise: every action necessarily has an agent (fā'il) in reality. If the agent is not a body (i.e., not a human or physical entity), then it must be God. He then distinguishes between being an agent and being an acquirer: an action does not require an acquirer (muktasib) in the same way it requires an agent. If an action is called 'acquisition' (kasb) by virtue of human involvement, it is still God who truly brings it about. The author uses the analogy of involuntary movement (al-ḥaraka al-iḍṭirāriyya): such movement indicates that God is its true agent, not the person who undergoes it. That person is 'moved' (mutaḥarrik) because the movement occurs in him, but he is not its agent. Likewise, for voluntary acts called kasb, the action indicates a true agent (God), but does not imply that the acquirer is that agent. The reason is that acquisition involves a power (qudra) that is created (muḥdatha) and belongs to the human. It is impossible for God to be described as having a created power, so He cannot be an 'acquirer' in the technical sense, even though He is the true creator of the act.

Key Terms
فاعل
مكتسب
كسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is necessary for every action?
A) An acquirer
B) An agent
C) A body
D) A created power

Key Takeaway
Every action requires a true agent; if that agent is not a physical body, it must be God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you truly believe that God is the agent of that action? How does that affect your understanding of your own responsibility and your plea for forgiveness?
?
If every good deed you do is ultimately caused by God, what does that mean for your pride and sense of self-righteousness? Will you let this truth humble you today?
?
How would your daily actions change if you constantly reminded yourself that God is the real doer, and you are only an acquirer? Are you ready to surrender the illusion of control and live in total dependence on Him?
