Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Quran 9:42 proves that ability (istita'a) can exist before action, contradicting Al-Ash'ari's view that ability is simultaneous with action.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows that the verse only refers to financial ability, not bodily ability. He agrees that financial means can precede action; it is bodily ability that is simultaneous.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse does not support the claim that bodily ability precedes action; it refers to financial resources, which can indeed precede action.

?
Al-Ash'ari insists that bodily ability does not precede action. Interpreting 'who cannot afford' in 58:4
Al-Ash'ari answers a question about inability and feeding sixty poor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari interprets the phrase 'فمن لم يستطع' in Surah Al-Mujadilah, distinguishing real incapacity from other forms of inability.

Core Idea
Incapacity in the Qur'an means real inability, not a metaphorical escape.

This lesson examines a brief but crucial passage from al-Ash'ari's Al-Luma' where he clarifies the meaning of 'inability' in the expiation for ẓihār. The questioner asks about the phrase 'whoever cannot afford' (فمن لم يستطع) in verse 58:4, and al-Ash'ari's answer pins down the exact nature of that inability. As you read, notice how the author insists on a literal reading—guarding against misinterpretations that could dilute the command.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a question is posed, then the answer begins with 'أَنَّ'.
2
Identify the key term
Focus on the phrase 'لِعَجْزٍ' (due to incapacity). Why does al-Ash'ari add this specification? What does it rule out?
3
Reflect on the broader significance
Consider how this interpretation protects the rigour of the expiation. Without this precision, one might mistakenly think any difficulty excuses the requirement.

Source Text

ومن سأل عن قوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا﴾ [المجادلة: ٤]؟ فالجواب: أَنَّ مَنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ لِعَجْزٍ، فَعَلَيْهِ إِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مِسْكِينًا.

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer about interpreting verse 58:4. The questioner asks about the meaning of 'whoever cannot afford' in the context of the expiation for ẓihār. Al-Ash'ari explains that the 'inability' here refers to literal incapacity due to lack of means, and such a person must then perform the alternative of feeding sixty poor people. The answer is straightforward, clarifying that the inability is a real inability, not a metaphorical one. This guards against misinterpretations that might extend the concession unnecessarily.

Key Takeaway

Al-Ash'ari's Contextual Interpretation of Quran 65:7
Al-Ash'ari interprets 'mā ātāhā' in 65:7 as financial provision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses the immediate context of Quran 65:7 to specify that 'what He has given' refers to financial provision for spending.

Core Idea
Context determines meaning: spending burden is tied to provision.

Al-Ash'ari often uses the immediate context of a verse to resolve interpretive questions. Here, a questioner asks about the meaning of "God does not burden a soul except with what He has given it." Al-Ash'ari responds by pointing to the adjacent verses about spending in divorce. This lesson follows his tafsir method.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Note the question and al-Ash'ari's response.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the question and answer
What is the question? How does al-Ash'ari define 'what He has given'? He specifies it as financial provision for spending.
3
Notice the contextual evidence
Al-Ash'ari says the verse was revealed immediately after the mention of spending. Look at the surrounding verses to see this.
Quran 65:7 is preceded by commands to spend according to means.
4
Reflect on the interpretive principle
This shows that the meaning of a verse can be clarified by its placement. Why is this important?
It prevents misapplication of the verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن سأل عن قوله تعالى: ﴿لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا مَا آتَاهَا﴾ [الطلاق: ٧]؟ فالمعنى: أَنَّهُ لَا يُكَلِّفُهَا مِنَ النَّفَقَةِ إِلَّا مَا آتَاهَا؛ لِأَنَّهُ قَالَ ذَلِكَ عَقِيبَ ذِكْرِ النَّفَقَةِ. قَالَ: ﴿وَمَنْ قُدِرَ عَلَيْهِ رِزْقُهُ فَلْيُنفِقْ مِمَّا آتَاهُ اللهُ لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا﴾ [الطلاق: ٧].
And whoever asks about His – exalted is He – saying: 'God does not burden a soul except [with] what He has given it' [al-Ṭalāq 7]? The meaning: that He does not burden it from spending except what He has given it, because He said that immediately after the mention of spending. He said: 'And whoever has his sustenance limited – let him spend from what God has given him. God does not burden a soul' [al-Ṭalāq 7].
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is another question-and-answer about interpreting a Quranic verse. The verse 'la yukallifu nafsan illā mā ātāhā' (God does not burden a soul except with what He has given it) is found in the context of divorce and spending on wives. Al-Ash'ari explains that the 'given' refers to provisions, specifically the financial ability to spend. He supports this by noting that the verse immediately follows the command for the wealthy and the poor to spend according to their means. Thus, the burden of spending is proportioned to what God has provided. This interpretation prevents misunderstanding that the verse might apply to all obligations irrespective of capacity.

Key Terms
تكليف
نفقة
آتى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'what He has given' refers to all abilities or talents, implying God only burdens people with tasks they can do.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari specifies that in this context, 'what He has given' means financial provision for spending, as shown by the surrounding verses.

Checkpoint
How does al-Ash'ari determine that 'mā ātāhā' in 65:7 refers specifically to spending?
A) He cites a Prophetic tradition
B) He says the verse is immediately preceded by mention of spending
C) He uses a linguistic argument
D) He says it is a general principle

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari shows that a verse's meaning is often clarified by its immediate context, here linking burden to spending.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a financial obligation you feel you cannot meet, do you truly believe that Allah only burdens you with what He has given you? How does this truth either comfort you or expose a lack of trust in His provision?
?
This lesson shows that reading a verse in its context changes its meaning. In what area of your life have you taken a Quranic verse out of context to justify leniency or severity? Will you commit to studying verses within their context before applying them?
?
If you are currently struggling to fulfill a duty because of limited resources, what concrete step can you take today to trust that Allah's provision is exactly what you need to carry that burden?

Divine Lenience: Interpreting 'Within Its Capacity' (2:286)
Al-Ash'ari explains divine lenience for inner thoughts and the meaning of 'capacity'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's explanation that God does not burden the soul with eliminating evil thoughts, and that 'capacity' means what is not unduly constricting or what is permissible.

Core Idea
God pardons evil thoughts; only actions are within the burden.

This lesson explores al-Ash'ari's response to a question about the famous Quranic verse 'God does not burden a soul except within its capacity.' The passage clarifies the scope of divine lenience, particularly regarding inner thoughts that incline toward sin. Al-Ash'ari teaches that capacity refers to what is manageable, not what is constricting, and he reports a companion's interpretation that it also means what is lawful.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how al-Ash'ari structures his response: he first identifies what God does NOT burden the soul with (removing evil thoughts), then explains the meaning of 'capacity' as non-constriction.
The passage begins with a question from an interlocutor.
2
Understand the concept of 'capacity'
Consider why 'capacity' is defined as what does not constrict. Al-Ash'ari emphasizes that God's commands are always doable without extreme difficulty. Reflect on the contrast between the earlier stricter obligation and the current lenience.
3
Examine the companion's interpretation
The passage ends with an alternative view from 'some of our companions' that 'capacity' means what is permissible and lawful. Compare this to the first interpretation and think about how both emphasize limitation of burden.
This shows the Ash'ari school's flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن سأل عن قوله تعالى: ﴿لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا﴾ [البقرة: ٢٨٦]؟ فالجواب عن ذلك: أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى لَا يُكَلِّفُهَا مَا يُضَيِّقُ عَلَيْهَا مِنْ إِزَالَةِ الْخَوَاطِرِ عَنِ النُّفُوسِ الَّتِي تَدْعُو إِلَى الشَّرِّ؛ لِأَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى قَدْ تَجَاوَزَ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، وَوَسَّعَ عَلَى الْمُسْلِمِينَ فِيمَا تَدْعُوهُمْ نُفُوسُهُمْ إِلَيْهِ مِنَ الْمَعْصِيَةِ، إِذَا لَمْ يَرْتَكِبُوا ذَلِكَ، بَعْدَ أَنْ كَانَ ذَلِكَ مُضَيَّقًا عَلَيْهِمْ. فَمَعْنَى ﴿لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا﴾ يَعْنِي: إِلَّا مَا لَمْ يُضَيِّقْهُ عَلَيْهَا؛ لِأَنَّ مَا أَمَرَ اللهُ تَعَالَى بِهِ عِبَادَهُ، لَا يَضِيقُ فِعْلُهُ، وَلَا يَعْجَزُونَ عَنْ الْإِتْيَانِ بِهِ. وَقَدْ قَالَ بَعْضُ أَصْحَابِنَا: ﴿لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا﴾ يَعْنِي: إِلَّا مَا يَسَعُهَا وَيَحِلُّ لَهَا.
And whoever asks about His – exalted is He – saying: 'God does not burden a soul except within its capacity' [al-Baqarah 286]? The answer about that: that God – exalted is He – does not burden it with what would constrict it, such as removing thoughts from the souls that call to evil, because God – exalted is He – has pardoned that and made it easy for the Muslims concerning what their souls call them to of disobedience, when they do not commit it, after that had been constricted upon them. So the meaning of 'God does not burden a soul except within its capacity' means: except what He did not constrict upon it, because what God – exalted is He – commands His servants, its performance is not constricting, nor are they incapable of performing it. And some of our companions have said: 'God does not burden a soul except within its capacity' means: except what is within its capacity and permissible for it.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer about the interpretation of verse 2:286, 'God does not burden a soul except within its capacity'. Al-Ash'ari addresses a specific concern: does this mean God does not require removing evil thoughts from the soul? He explains that God does not burden people with what is constricting, such as eliminating the inner inclinations toward sin, because God has pardoned evil thoughts unless acted upon. Thus, 'capacity' means what is not beyond one's ability to perform without undue strain. He supports this by noting that God's commands are always within human capability. Finally, he reports an alternative interpretation from some of his companions: 'capacity' means what is lawful and suitable for the person. This guards against extreme spiritual demands that were previously imposed.

Key Terms
وسع
تضييق
خواطر
تجاوز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'within its capacity' includes the ability to completely suppress evil thoughts.
Correction: The author says only actual sin is forbidden; evil thoughts are pardoned unless acted upon.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari's explanation of verse 2:286, what does God NOT burden the soul with?
A) Performing obligatory prayers
B) Removing evil thoughts from the soul
C) Spending in charity
D) Fasting in Ramadan

Key Takeaway
God's mercy frees believers from being accountable for fleeting evil thoughts, limiting obligation to what is feasible and lawful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When an evil thought enters your mind, do you immediately feel guilty, thinking you have already sinned? How does this verse's explanation—that God pardons such thoughts—change how you see your own accountability? Will you now respond with gratitude rather than despair?
?
Think of a religious command you have struggled with, perhaps thinking it's 'too much' for you. According to this lesson, what does 'within your capacity' truly mean? Can you honestly say that command is impossible, or just difficult? What step will you take this week to act on that command, trusting God has made it possible?
?
Have you ever used the excuse 'it's beyond my capacity' to avoid a duty you simply disliked? How does al-Ash'ari's distinction between 'not constricting' and 'permissible' confront that excuse? What would it cost you to obey fully, and are you willing to pay that price?

Interpreting the ifrit's claim of strength in 27:39
Al-Ash'ari explains two possible meanings of the ifrit's claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari reconciles the ifrit's claim of personal strength with the Ash'ari doctrine that all power comes from God.

Core Idea
The ifrit's strength is not independent but created by God at the moment of intention.

This passage addresses a potential objection: if the ifrit claimed to be strong and trustworthy to bring the throne, does that imply independent power? Al-Ash'ari offers two careful interpretations that preserve both the truthfulness of the ifrit and the Ash'ari principle that God creates all actions and abilities. Let's see how he does it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal English translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if the ifrit was truthful...' and 'if he was one of those...'.
The passage is a response to a questioner.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Identify the two interpretations al-Ash'ari provides. The first: if the ifrit is truthful, his claim means he would be able if he undertakes and intends. The second: if his ability is created by God at the moment of intention, he is not a liar.
The second interpretation directly preserves Ash'ari theology.
3
Understand the theological significance
Reflect on why this interpretation matters: it defends the doctrine of kasb (acquisition) and shows that any power a creature claims is ultimately created by God. This prevents attributing independent power to creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن سأل عن قول الله تعالى مخبرًا عن العفريت: ﴿وَإِنِّي عَلَيْهِ لَقَوِيٌّ أَمِينٌ﴾ [النمل: ٣٩]؟ فَإِنْ كَانَ الْعِفْرِيتُ صَادِقًا فَالْمَعْنَى فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَإِنِّي عَلَيْهِ لَقَوِيٌّ أَمِينٌ﴾ إِنْ تَكَلَّفْتُ ذَلِكَ وَأَرَدْتُهُ. وَإِنْ كَانَ مِمَّنْ إِذَا أَرَادَ ذَلِكَ أَحْدَثَ اللهُ تَعَالَى لَهُ الْقُدْرَةَ عَلَيْهِ لَمْ يَكُنْ كَاذِبًا.
And whoever asks about God's – exalted is He – statement, informing about the ifrit: 'And indeed I am, for it, strong and trustworthy' [al-Naml 39]? So if the ifrit was truthful, then the meaning in his statement 'And indeed I am, for it, strong and trustworthy' is: if I undertake that and intend it. And if he was one of those who, when he intends that, God – exalted is He – creates the ability for him, then he would not be a liar.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer regarding the ifrit's claim in the story of Solomon (Sulaymān) that he could bring the throne of Bilqīs before Solomon stood up. The questioner raises a potential issue: if the ifrit claimed strength (quwwah) in himself, does that conflict with the Ashʿarī position that all power is from God? Al-Ashʿarī resolves this by offering two possible interpretations based on whether the ifrit was truthful. First, if he was truthful, his claim means that he would have the ability if he undertook the task and willed it, i.e., he had the strength to carry it out. Second, if he was among those for whom God creates ability at the moment of intention, then his statement is not a lie, because God would indeed create the power for him. This preserves both the truthfulness of the ifrit (if he was truthful) and the Ashʿarī doctrine of the creation of actions by God.

Key Terms
عفريت
قوي
أمين
قدرة
تكلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the ifrit's claim attributes independent power to himself, conflicting with God's sole creative power.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari shows the ifrit's strength is either contingent on his undertaking or created by God at the moment of intention, so it does not imply independent power.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ash'ari, in the second interpretation, how does the ifrit become able to bring the throne?
A) He has inherent power
B) God creates the ability for him when he intends it
C) He was lying about his strength
D) He performs a miracle

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's interpretation preserves both the ifrit's truthfulness and the doctrine that God creates all abilities at the moment of intention.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you claim to be 'strong' or 'able' in any area of life, do you truly believe that God creates that ability at the moment of your intention? Or do you secretly think the power resides permanently within you? How would your daily reliance on Him change if you lived the first belief?
?
Think of a task you feel completely incapable of right now. According to this lesson, if you sincerely intend it, God may create the ability for you then. What would you dare to attempt if you believed this with certainty?
?
The ifrit's statement was truthful only because he acknowledged God's creation of ability. In what area of your life are you most tempted to attribute success solely to your own inherent strength, forgetting that the power was given at that moment? What concrete step can you take today to shift that attribution back to Allah?

Objection on Capacity and Ash'ari's Interpretation
Ash'ari addresses an objection and interprets the verse on divine burden.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari resolves the objection regarding capacity for disobedience and interprets the verse 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity' as meaning that commands are not made difficult.

Core Idea
Divine commands are always within human capability; difficulty is removed.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari tackles an objection concerning human capacity (istita'a) in relation to acts of disobedience. He explains that Allah has made disobedience easy in terms of inclination but not in action, and then interprets the key Qur'anic verse to mean that Allah only commands what is not made difficult. This lesson unpacks that interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The passage begins by addressing an objection about capacity and disobedience. Notice how Ash'ari responds that Allah eased the inclination but not the act.
2
Understand Ash'ari's interpretation
Focus on the meaning of 'وسعها' as 'ما لم يضيقه عليها' (what is not made difficult). This emphasizes that divine commands are attainable.
3
Connect to the wider doctrine
Reflect that this interpretation supports the Ash'ari position that human capacity is created by Allah and that obligations are always feasible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استشكال على مقارنة الاستطاعة للفعل. قد تجاوز عن ذلك، ووسَّعَ على المسلمين فيما تدعوهم نفوسهم إليه من المعصية، إذا لم يرتكبوا ذلك، بعد أن كان ذلك مُضيَّقًا عليهم. فمعنى وَلَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا [البقرة : ٢٨٦] يعني : إِلَّا ما لم يضيقه عليها ؛ لأنَّ ما أمر الله - تعالى - به عبادَه ، لا يَضِيقُ فعله، ولا يعجزون عن الإتيان به. وقد قال بعض أصحابنا : لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا يعني: إلا ما يَسَعُها ويَحِلُّ لَها .
Objection on comparing capacity to the act. He has pardoned that, and made easy for the Muslims what their souls call them to of disobedience, if they do not commit it, after that was made difficult for them. So the meaning of 'And Allah does not burden a soul except [with what is within] its capacity' [Al-Baqarah: 286] means: except what is not made difficult for it; because what Allah Almighty commands His servants, its doing is not difficult, nor are they incapable of performing it. And some of our companions said: 'Allah does not burden a soul except [with what is within] its capacity' means: except what is permissible and lawful for it.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection concerning the comparison of human capacity (istita'a) to the act of disobedience. The author begins by stating that Allah has pardoned and made easy for Muslims what their souls incline to of sin, provided they do not actually commit it, even though it was previously made difficult. Then he interprets the Qur'anic verse 'Allah does not burden a soul except [with what is within] its capacity' (2:286). He explains that this means Allah only imposes what is not made difficult for the person, because whatever Allah commands, its performance is not difficult and they are not incapable of it. Some of the author's companions add an interpretation: 'what is within its capacity' means what is permissible (yasu'uha) and lawful (yahillu laha) for it. This clarifies that divine obligation is always within human capability, and that Allah's facilitation precedes the act.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة
الكلفة
الوسع
التضييق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse implies that humans have a pre-existing capacity for any action before it occurs.
Correction: Ash'ari explains that 'capacity' here refers to Allah not making the command difficult; capacity is created by Allah at the time of action.

Checkpoint
According to Ash'ari in this passage, what does 'وسعها' in the verse 'لا يكلف الله نفسا إلا وسعها' mean?
A) Only actions that are easy are commanded.
B) Allah does not command anything beyond what the person can bear, and it is not made difficult.
C) Only permissible actions are commanded.
D) Disobedience is never commanded.

Key Takeaway
Divine commands are always within human capacity because Allah does not make them difficult.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a divine command you have been avoiding or struggling with. According to this lesson, the difficulty is not from Allah—so where is it coming from? What would it cost you to take that command seriously starting today?
?
Do you ever use the excuse 'I cannot' to postpone obedience? This lesson declares that Allah never commands beyond capacity. Which specific obligation are you neglecting, and what step can you take right now to remove the imagined difficulty?
?
If you truly believed that every command of Allah is within your ability, what would change about your daily worship, your treatment of others, and your patience in trials? Be specific.

Alternate Interpretation: Capacity as Permissibility
Companions of Ash'ari offer a permission-based interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the alternate interpretation by some Ash'ari scholars that 'capacity' in the verse refers to what is permissible and lawful.

Core Idea
Divine burden is limited to what is permissible; disobedience is not commanded.

Some of Imam al-Ash'ari's companions offered a different nuance for the same verse. They explained that 'capacity' means what is permissible and lawful (yasu'uha wa yahillu laha). This lesson explores that interpretation and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the alternative interpretation
The passage states that some companions said 'وسعها' means 'ما يسعها ويحل لها' (what is permissible and lawful for it).
2
Understand the nuance
This interpretation shifts the focus from capability to lawfulness: God only commands what is permissible, not what is prohibited.
3
Compare with Ash'ari's interpretation
Note the difference: Ash'ari emphasized feasibility, while his companions emphasized permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استشكال على مقارنة الاستطاعة للفعل. قد تجاوز عن ذلك، ووسَّعَ على المسلمين فيما تدعوهم نفوسهم إليه من المعصية، إذا لم يرتكبوا ذلك، بعد أن كان ذلك مُضيَّقًا عليهم. فمعنى وَلَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا [البقرة : ٢٨٦] يعني : إِلَّا ما لم يضيقه عليها ؛ لأنَّ ما أمر الله - تعالى - به عبادَه ، لا يَضِيقُ فعله، ولا يعجزون عن الإتيان به. وقد قال بعض أصحابنا : لَا يُكَلِّفُ اللَّهُ نَفْسًا إِلَّا وُسْعَهَا يعني: إلا ما يَسَعُها ويَحِلُّ لَها .
Objection on comparing capacity to the act. He has pardoned that, and made easy for the Muslims what their souls call them to of disobedience, if they do not commit it, after that was made difficult for them. So the meaning of 'And Allah does not burden a soul except [with what is within] its capacity' [Al-Baqarah: 286] means: except what is not made difficult for it; because what Allah Almighty commands His servants, its doing is not difficult, nor are they incapable of performing it. And some of our companions said: 'Allah does not burden a soul except [with what is within] its capacity' means: except what is permissible and lawful for it.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection concerning the comparison of human capacity (istita'a) to the act of disobedience. The author begins by stating that Allah has pardoned and made easy for Muslims what their souls incline to of sin, provided they do not actually commit it, even though it was previously made difficult. Then he interprets the Qur'anic verse 'Allah does not burden a soul except [with what is within] its capacity' (2:286). He explains that this means Allah only imposes what is not made difficult for the person, because whatever Allah commands, its performance is not difficult and they are not incapable of it. Some of the author's companions add an interpretation: 'what is within its capacity' means what is permissible (yasu'uha) and lawful (yahillu laha) for it. This clarifies that divine obligation is always within human capability, and that Allah's facilitation precedes the act.

Key Terms
الوسع
الحل
اليسع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse means that any command, even if sinful, is within human capacity.
Correction: The companions' interpretation clarifies that 'capacity' here refers to what is permissible and lawful, so commands only cover halal actions, not sinful ones.

Checkpoint
According to the companions' interpretation, what does 'وسعها' refer to?
A) What is easy
B) What is permissible and lawful
C) What is possible
D) What is not difficult

Key Takeaway
Capacity (wus') also refers to permissibility; God only commands what is lawful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you blame your circumstances or your own choice? This lesson says Allah never commands what is unlawful—so your disobedience is never because He made it your only option. Will you stop excusing your sins as 'beyond your control' and take full responsibility?
?
If you truly believed that every command from Allah is within what is lawful for you, would you still hesitate to obey? What would change in your life right now if you acted on that certainty?
?
The verse limits what Allah asks of you to what is permissible. Does your heart feel gratitude for His mercy, or do you still resent His commands? Examine yourself: are you obeying out of love or reluctance?

The Mu'tazila Claim from the Ifrit Verse
Ash'ari presents the Mu'tazila argument and dismisses it as evil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila used the Ifrit's statement to argue for capacity before the act and why Ash'ari considers this argument invalid.

Core Idea
The Ifrit's words are not proof for religion; Mu'tazila misuse them.

The Mu'tazila cited the Ifrit's statement in Surah An-Naml to support their doctrine that capacity (istita'a) exists before the act. They argued that Prophet Sulayman did not contradict the Ifrit, proving his truthfulness. Ash'ari refutes this by first questioning the premise and then showing the Ifrit's words are ambiguous.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and translation. Notice how Ash'ari introduces the verse and the Mu'tazila interpretation.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila argument
Find the claim that Sulayman's silence indicates the Ifrit's truthfulness, and how they link this to capacity before the act.
3
Analyze Ash'ari's initial response
Ash'ari points out that the Ifrit's words are not evidence for religion and that the Mu'tazila are building on falsehood.
4
Consider the broader implication
This lesson sets the stage for Ash'ari's detailed refutation in the next lesson.

ومَنْ سأل عن قول الله - تعالى - مُخبرًا عَنِ العِفْرِيت : ﴿وَإِنِّي عَلَيْهِ لَقَوِيُّ أَمِينُ ﴾ [النمل: ٣٩]؟ فإن كان العفريتُ صادِقًا فالمعنى في قوله: ﴿وَإِنِّي عَلَيْهِ لَقَوِيٌّ أَمِينُ ﴾ [النمل: ٣٩] إن تكلَّفْتُ ذلك وأَرَدْتُه . وَإِنْ كان ممَّنْ إذا أرادَ ذلك أحدث الله - تعالى - لَه القدرة علَيْه لم يكن كاذبا . وإنْ لم يقل هذا القولَ على هذا المعْنَى فهو كاذِبٌ. وليس في قول العفاريت والشياطين حُجَّةٌ على دِينِ ربِّ العالمين. وزَعَمتِ المعتزلةُ أنَّ العِفريت لم يُكذِّبُه سُلَيْمانُ، وهُوَ نَبِيٌّ من أنبياء الله - تعالى - على قولِهِ : أَنَا عَانِيكَ بِهِ قَبْلَ أَن تَقُومَ مِن مَّقَامِكَ وَإِنِّي عَلَيْهِ لَقَوِيٌّ أَمِينُ ﴾ [النمل: ۳۹] ، ولا يجوز لأحدٍ أن يكذِبَ بينَ يَدَيْ نبيِّ . وهُوَ يَعلَمُ أنَّه إذَا كَذَبَ ، رَدَّ اللهُ عليه كذبه، على لسان النبي -صلى الله عليه - كما قالَ لنبيه : ﴿ إِذَا جَاءَكَ الْمُنَافِقُونَ ﴾ [المنافقون: ١] الآيةَ ، فأَخْبَرَ الله - تعالى بكذبهم ، ومثل ذلك في القُرآنِ كثير . واحْتَجوا بذلك أنَّ الاستطاعة قبل الفعل، فبئسَ مَا قالُوا وظنُّوا ، بل سَوَّلَتْ لهم أنفسُهُم الأَباطيل . فالجواب : أنَّا نقول لمن احتج علينا بذلك : إنَّه ليست تخلُو هذه الآيةُ التي حكاها الله - تعالى - عن العِفريتِ أنْ يكونَ العِفريتُ عنى بقوله: ﴿وَإِنِّي عَلَيْهِ لَقَوِيٌّ أَمِينُ ﴾ [النمل: ٣٩] إِنِ اسْتَطَعْتُ ذَلِكَ وتكلَّفتُه ،وأردتُه ، أو يكونَ عَنَى بقوله: ﴿وَإِنِّي عَلَيْهِ لَقَوِيٌّ أَمِينُ ﴾ [النمل: ٣٩] إن شاء الله . أَوْ يكونَ عنى بقوله : إن قوَّاني الله - تعالى - عَلَيْهِ . ولو لم يَعلَمْ سُليمانُ أنَّ العِفريتَ أَضمر شيئًا من ذلك لكَذَّبَه ، وردَّ عليه قولَه .
And whoever asks about the saying of Allah Almighty informing about the Ifrit: 'And indeed I am for it strong, trustworthy' [An-Naml: 39]? If the Ifrit was truthful, then the meaning of his saying: 'And indeed I am for it strong, trustworthy' [An-Naml: 39] is: if I undertake that and intend it. And if he was one of those who, if he intends that, Allah Almighty creates for him the ability upon it, he would not be a liar. And if he did not say this saying with this meaning, then he is a liar. And there is no proof in the saying of the 'afarit and devils upon the religion of the Lord of the worlds. And the Mu'tazila claimed that the Ifrit was not contradicted by Sulayman, and he is a prophet of the prophets of Allah Almighty, based on his saying: 'I will bring it to you before you rise from your place, and indeed I am for it strong, trustworthy' [An-Naml: 39], and it is not permissible for anyone to lie before a prophet. And he knows that if he lies, Allah refutes his lie on the tongue of the prophet - may Allah bless him and grant him peace - as He said to His prophet: 'When the hypocrites come to you' [Al-Munafiqun: 1] the verse, so Allah Almighty informed of their lie, and similar to that in the Qur'an is much. And they argued by that that capacity is before the act; how evil is what they said and thought! Rather, their souls embellished falsehoods for them. So the answer: We say to whoever argues against us with that: This verse that Allah Almighty related from the Ifrit cannot be but that the Ifrit meant by his saying: 'And indeed I am for it strong, trustworthy' [An-Naml: 39] 'if I am able to do that and undertake it and intend it,' or he meant by his saying: 'And indeed I am for it strong, trustworthy' [An-Naml: 39] 'if Allah wills,' or he meant by his saying: 'if Allah strengthens me upon it.' And if Sulayman did not know that the Ifrit implied any of that, he would have contradicted him and rejected his statement.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Mu'tazila argument based on the verse about the Ifrit in Surah An-Naml (39). The author first presents a preliminary analysis: if the Ifrit is truthful, his statement 'I am strong, trustworthy' must be interpreted as conditional on his undertaking and intention, or that Allah creates ability for him. If he did not mean that, he would be a liar. Then the author dismisses the Ifrit's words as proof for religion. The Mu'tazila claim that the Ifrit was not contradicted by Prophet Sulayman, and since a prophet would refute a liar, this proves the Ifrit was truthful, and they use this to argue that capacity (istita'a) exists before the act. The author condemns this reasoning as evil. Then the answer: the verse is open to multiple interpretations—the Ifrit may have meant 'if I am able and undertake it,' 'if Allah wills,' or 'if Allah gives me strength.' If Sulayman had not known that the Ifrit intended one of these meanings, he would have refuted him. Thus, the verse does not prove that capacity is prior to the act.

Key Terms
العفريت
المعتزلة
الاستطاعة
التكذيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ifrit's statement that he is 'strong, trustworthy' proves that humans have inherent capacity to act before the act itself.
Correction: Ash'ari shows the statement is conditional and that the Ifrit's speech is not evidence in religion; the Mu'tazila wrongly assume Sulayman's silence indicates truthfulness, but the verse could be interpreted multiple ways.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazila argument presented, why did Prophet Sulayman not contradict the Ifrit?
A) Because the Ifrit was actually a believer.
B) Because the Ifrit was truthful and Sulayman knew it.
C) Because Sulayman was unaware of the Ifrit's lie.
D) Because the Ifrit was too powerful.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila misuse the Ifrit verse to support their doctrine of capacity before the act, but Ash'ari dismisses their reasoning as invalid and based on false assumptions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever accepted a religious argument simply because it seemed convenient or supported your existing view, without critically examining its source? What cost did that have for your sincerity? Will you commit to examining every proof you rely on, even if it means letting go of a comfortable position?
?
The Mu'tazila built a doctrine on the word of an 'ifrit. Where in your own life have you used questionable evidence or reasoning to justify a belief or action? What would it look like to repent from that and seek the truth solely from Allah and His revelation?
?
Imagine standing before Allah with arguments that were used to mislead others. The Ash'ari here pronounces 'how evil is what they said and thought.' Does that warning pierce your heart? Are you willing to interrogate your own convictions today, asking Allah to purify them from falsehood, no matter how dear they are?

Ash'ari's Refutation: Alternative Interpretations
Ash'ari gives the answer: the Ifrit's statement is conditional.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ash'ari's response to the Mu'tazila: the Ifrit's statement can be interpreted in multiple ways, none of which support the claim of capacity before the act.

Core Idea
The verse is ambiguous; it does not prove capacity before the act.

Having condemned the Mu'tazila argument, Ash'ari now provides a detailed refutation. He shows that the Ifrit's statement is open to several legitimate interpretations—none of which imply that capacity exists before the act. If Sulayman had known the Ifrit intended a false meaning, he would have contradicted him.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer
Read the Arabic and translation of Ash'ari's response.
2
Identify the three interpretations
Notice the three possible meanings Ash'ari offers for the Ifrit's statement.
3
Understand the implication
Ash'ari argues that Sulayman's silence does not prove truthfulness because the Ifrit may have implied a conditional meaning.
4
Connect to the broader debate
This lesson shows how Ash'ari refutes the Mu'tazila by showing the verse does not support their doctrine.

Proof from Yajuj and Majuj: Ability is With the Act
Al-Ash'ari proves that ability exists only with the act using the story of Yajuj and Majuj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari uses the Qur'anic story of Yajuj and Majuj to demonstrate that human ability does not precede the act but exists only concurrently with it by Allah's will.

Core Idea
Ability is not prior to action; it arises with the act through divine will.

In classical Islamic theology, the relationship between human ability and divine will is central. Al-Ash'ari here presents a unique proof from the story of Dhul-Qarnayn's wall and the nations of Yajuj and Majuj. By examining the tafsir consensus on their failed attempts and eventual success, he argues that ability cannot be possessed before an act – it is only present at the moment of action, contingent on Allah's will. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and translation
Read the Qur'anic verse (18:97) and its literal translation. Notice the key term 'istita'a' and its absence before their success.
The verse itself does not mention 'in sha Allah,' but the tafsir explains the background.
2
Understand the tafsir consensus
According to unanimous interpretation, Yajuj and Majuj tried daily to breach the wall but failed because they neglected to say 'if Allah wills.' On the appointed day, they said it and succeeded. This shows that ability came only when they acknowledged divine will.
The consensus among monotheists is highlighted by al-Ash'ari to strengthen his argument.
3
Connect to the theological conclusion
Al-Ash'ari concludes that they had no ability before the act. Ability exists only concurrently with the act, by Allah's will. Reflect on how this refutes the view that ability precedes action.
This conclusion is central to the Ash'ari position on kasb (acquisition).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل فى ذلك قول الله - تعالى -: ﴿فَمَا أَسْطَاعُوا أَن يَظْهَرُوهُ وَمَا أَسَتَطَاعُواْ لَهُ نَقْبا﴾ [الكهف: ٩٧] . وقَدْ جاءَ في التفسير ، لا خُلفَ بين أحدٍ من الموحدين فيه ، أنهم كانوا في كلِّ يومٍ يَأْمَلُونَ أَن يُصبِحُوا وَقَدْ فتحوه، فلا يقولونَ: إِنْ شاءَ اللَّهُ ، فإذا كان اليوم المقدر قالُوا : إن شاءَ الله، فأضحوا وقد فتحوه . فدلَّ أنْ لا استطاعةَ لهم قبلَ الفِعْلِ . إلا مع الفِعْلِ للفِعْلِ، بإرادة الله ذلك .
And the proof of that is the statement of Allah: 'So they (Ya'juj and Ma'juj) were not able to scale it, nor were they able to dig through it.' [al-Kahf 97]. And it has come in the interpretation, concerning which there is no disagreement among any of the monotheists, that they used every day to hope that they would wake up having opened it, and they did not say 'if Allah wills.' Then when the appointed day came, they said 'if Allah wills,' so they woke up having opened it. So this indicates that they have no ability before the act, except along with the act for the act, by the will of Allah.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This is a proof passage. Al-Ash'ari cites a Qur'anic verse about the wall built by Dhul-Qarnayn to contain Ya'juj and Ma'juj. According to unanimous exegesis, they tried daily to breach it but failed because they neglected to say 'if Allah wills.' On the predestined day, they said 'if Allah wills' and succeeded. This demonstrates that they lacked ability before the act; ability occurred only with the act, by Allah's will. The conclusion is clear: ability (istita'a) is not prior to the act but concurrent with it, subject to divine will.

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
الاستطاعة
المشيئة
التفسير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That saying 'in sha Allah' is merely a ritual phrase without affecting outcome.
Correction: The story shows it reflects reliance on divine will for ability; ability is not present without acknowledgment of Allah's will.

Checkpoint
What lesson does al-Ash'ari draw from the story of Ya'juj and Ma'juj?
A) They had full ability before the act
B) Ability is only with the act by Allah's will
C) Saying 'in sha' Allah' guarantees success
D) They were unable to breach the wall

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari proves that ability is not prior to action but arises simultaneously with the act by Allah's will, using the consensus on Yajuj and Majuj's failed attempts until they said 'in sha Allah'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your ability to perform even the smallest action comes from Allah alone, or do you secretly rely on your own strength? When you say 'in sha Allah,' is it a genuine acknowledgment of that dependence or just a habit?
?
Think of a time when you failed despite your best efforts. Could it be that you lacked the ability because Allah had not willed it? How does that change how you view your failures and your reliance on Him?
?
If ability is created only with the act, what does that mean for your excuses about procrastination? Are you waiting for ability to come before you act, or will you act trusting that Allah will give you the ability at that moment?

The First Quranic Proof: Capability Arises with Action
Al-Ash'ari's first Quranic proof: the story of Yajuj and Majuj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the story of Yajuj and Majuj (Surah al-Kahf 97) demonstrates that human capability to act is created by Allah at the moment of action, not before.

Core Idea
Capability is not a pre-existing power; it is created with the act.

In this lesson, we examine the first of three Quranic proofs cited by Al-Ash'ari to establish that capability (istita'a) does not exist before action but is created concurrently. The verse about Yajuj and Majuj shows that their repeated attempts failed until they said 'insha'Allah', indicating that capability to breach the barrier came only when Allah willed it.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic verse and its commentary
Open the passage and read the verse from Surah al-Kahf along with the interpretation that the people of the barrier never succeeded until they said 'insha'Allah'.
Notice the connection between saying 'insha'Allah' and the action becoming possible.
2
Identify the logical implication
Ask: Why does this story prove that capability is simultaneous with action? The answer is that before they said 'insha'Allah', they had no capability; after they said it, capability arose.
3
Reflect on the role of Allah's will
Understand that the verse shows that capability is given by Allah at the moment of action, not something inherent in human beings.
This refutes the view that humans have independent power.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استشكال على مقارنة الاستطاعة للفعل

والدليل فى ذلك قول الله - تعالى -: ﴿فَمَا أَسْطَاعُوا أَن يَظْهَرُوهُ وَمَا أَسَتَطَاعُواْ لَهُ نَقْبا﴾ [الكهف: ٩٧]. وقد جاء في التفسير، لا خلف بين أحد من الموحدين فيه، أنهم كانوا في كل يوم يأملون أن يصبحوا وقد فتحوه، فلا يقولون: إن شاء الله، فإذا كان اليوم المقدر قالوا: إن شاء الله، فأضحوا وقد فتحوه. فدل أن لا استطاعة لهم قبل الفعل إلا مع الفعل للفعل، بإرادة الله تعالى ذلك.

وقول الله تعالى في صاحب يوسف: ﴿فَأَنَسَنَهُ الشَّيْطَانُ ذِكْرَ رَبِّهِ، فَلَبِثَ فِي السِّجْنِ بِضْعَ سِنِينَ﴾ [يوسف: ٤٢]، يعني أنسى الشيطان الناجي أن يذكر يوسف عند الملك، فلم تكن للناجي استطاعة أن يذكر أمر يوسف للملك؛ إذ كان قد وعد يوسف بأن يذكره عند ربه قبل خروجه من السجن. وكان ذلك لتمام مراد الله تعالى بيوسف إلى الوقت المعلوم الذي رأى الملك فيه الرؤيا.

وأيضًا: قول الله تعالى لنبيه عليه السلام: ﴿وَلَا تَقُولَنَّ لِشَيْءٍ إِنِّي فَاعِلُ ذَلِكَ غَدًا إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللَّهُ﴾ [الكهف: ٢٣-٢٤]، فأمر الله تعالى نبيه بأن لا يقدم على فعل شيء يقع في نفسه ما يأتي، بأن يستثني في قوله، فأخبر الله تعالى نبيه أن لا يكون قولك هذا كائنا قبل فعلك له إلا إن أردت أنا ذلك، فسلم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لأمر الله تعالى.
An objection regarding the comparison of capability to the action. The proof for that is the saying of Allah, the Exalted: 'So they were not able to scale it, nor were they able to dig through it' [al-Kahf: 97]. And it has come in the commentary, with no dispute among any of the monotheists regarding it, that they used to every day hope that they would become and they had opened it, so they would not say: 'If Allah wills', but when the appointed day came, they said: 'If Allah wills', and they became and had opened it. So it indicates that there is no capability for them before the action except with the action for the action, by the will of Allah, the Exalted. And the saying of Allah, the Exalted, concerning the companion of Yusuf: 'Then Satan caused him to forget the mention of his Lord, so he remained in prison for several years' [Yusuf: 42], meaning Satan caused the survivor to forget to mention Yusuf before the king, so there was no capability for the survivor to mention the matter of Yusuf to the king, since he had promised Yusuf that he would mention him to his lord before his exit from prison. And that was for the completion of the will of Allah, the Exalted, concerning Yusuf until the appointed time in which the king saw the vision. And also: The saying of Allah, the Exalted, to His Prophet, peace be upon him: 'And never say of anything, "Indeed, I will do that tomorrow," except [when adding], "If Allah wills"' [al-Kahf: 23-24]. So Allah, the Exalted, commanded His Prophet not to proceed to do anything that occurs to his mind without excepting in his statement, and Allah, the Exalted, informed His Prophet that your statement this would not be existent before your doing it unless I will that. So the Prophet, peace be upon him, submitted to the command of Allah, the Exalted.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a proof (istidlal) using three Quranic verses to demonstrate that human capability (istita'a) is not present before an action but is created by Allah concurrently with the action. The author begins by noting an objection (istishkal) concerning the comparison of capability to the action, then provides evidence. The first proof is from Surah al-Kahf about Yajuj and Majuj: they repeatedly failed to breach the barrier until they said 'insha'Allah', indicating that capability came only when Allah willed. The second proof is from Surah Yusuf: the companion who was saved forgot to mention Yusuf because Allah willed Yusuf to remain in prison; thus, he had no capability to remember. The third proof is the command to the Prophet to say 'insha'Allah' when intending future actions, showing that the action will not occur unless Allah wills it. The passage concludes that capability is dependent on Allah's will and is not inherent in the human agent prior to the act.

Key Terms
استطاعة (istita'a/capability)
استثناء (istithna'/exception)
فعل (fi'l/action)
إرادة (irada/will)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think humans have inherent capability to act independently of Allah's will.
Correction: This verse shows that even physical strength or effort does not yield results without Allah's concurrent creation of capability.

Checkpoint
What did the people of the barrier say on the appointed day that led to success?
A) 'We will succeed'
B) 'If Allah wills'
C) 'Tomorrow we will break through'
D) 'We are able'

Key Takeaway
Capability is not a pre-existing power; it is created by Allah at the moment of action, as demonstrated by the Yajuj and Majuj story.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make plans, do you genuinely feel that your success depends on Allah's will at that moment, or do you rely on your own abilities and forget to say 'If Allah wills'? What would change if you truly internalised that you have no capability except with Allah's action?
?
Think of a time you repeatedly failed at something. Did you acknowledge Allah's will in your efforts, or did you persist without turning to Him? How might saying 'insha'Allah' with full conviction alter your approach?
?
The Yajuj and Majuj story shows that capability is granted only at the appointed time by Allah. Is there an area in your life where you are impatiently striving without recognizing that Allah alone grants the ability to succeed? How can you surrender that area to His timing?

The Second Quranic Proof: Forgetting Shows Lack of Capability
Al-Ash'ari's second Quranic proof: the forgetfulness of Yusuf's companion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the story of Yusuf's companion who forgot to mention him demonstrates that capability to remember is not inherent but granted by Allah.

Core Idea
Forgetting is not just a lapse; it reflects lack of capability created by Allah.

Al-Ash'ari uses the story of the companion of Yusuf who forgot to mention Yusuf to the king as evidence that capability is not an independent human attribute. The companion had no capability to remember because Allah willed that Yusuf remain in prison until the appointed time.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its context
Open Surah Yusuf 42: 'Then Satan caused him to forget the mention of his Lord...'. Understand that the 'him' refers to the companion who was saved.
The companion promised to mention Yusuf but forgot.
2
Analyze the implication
Ask: Why does this prove that capability (istita'a) is not pre-existing? Because the companion had the intention but lacked the ability to remember. His capability to mention Yusuf was not present.
This shows that capability is not under human control but given by Allah.
3
Connect to Allah's will
Realize that this forgetting was part of Allah's decree to fulfill His will for Yusuf's imprisonment.
Capability is contingent upon divine will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Why did the companion of Yusuf fail to mention him to the king?
A) He deliberately withheld the information
B) He forgot due to Satan and Allah did not grant him capability to remember
C) He was afraid of the king
D) He did not want to help Yusuf

Key Takeaway
Capability is not an inherent human power; it is created by Allah at the moment of action, as shown by the companion's inability to remember.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a time you confidently promised something but then completely forgot or failed to deliver. Do you now see that your inability was from Allah? How does this realization humble your self-reliance?
?
Do you live as if your memory and abilities are fully under your control? How would your daily prayers change if you truly believed that even your ability to remember is a gift created by Allah at every moment?
?
The companion's forgetfulness served Allah's greater plan for Yusuf. Can you recall a personal failure or forgetfulness that later you understood was part of Allah's wisdom? How does this reshape your trust in His decree over your own plans?

The Third Quranic Proof: The Command to Say 'Insha'Allah'
Al-Ash'ari's third Quranic proof: the command to say 'insha'Allah'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic command to the Prophet to say 'insha'Allah' when planning future actions demonstrates that human capability is dependent on Allah's will, not on human intention.

Core Idea
Saying 'insha'Allah' acknowledges that capability comes only by Allah's will.

The third proof is a direct command from Allah to the Prophet: never say you will do something tomorrow without adding 'insha'Allah'. This teaches that any action we intend to perform does not become possible until Allah wills it. It reinforces that capability is not inherent but granted by Allah at the time of action.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse
Open Surah al-Kahf 23-24: 'And never say of anything, "Indeed, I will do that tomorrow," except [when adding], "If Allah wills."'
Note that this is a command to the Prophet, and by extension to all believers.
2
Understand the implication
The verse teaches that claiming certainty about future actions without linking them to Allah's will is incorrect. The action will only occur if Allah wills it.
This implies that the ability to perform the action is not under human control.
3
Relate to capability
Al-Ash'ari uses this to argue that if humans had inherent capability, they would not need to say 'insha'Allah' to guarantee the action. The need for the exception proves that capability is dependent on Allah's will.
Thus, capability is concurrent with action, not pre-existing.

Source Text

What does the verse in Surah al-Kahf 23-24 command the Prophet to do when planning future actions?
A) Plan carefully

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'insha'Allah' in your daily plans, do you truly feel that your ability to act depends on Allah's will in that moment? Reflect on a time you confidently said 'I will do it' without adding the exception—what does that reveal about your reliance on yourself? Commit to checking your intention tomorrow each time you speak.
?
The Prophet himself was commanded to say 'insha'Allah'. If the best of creation needed to acknowledge dependence, how can you possibly think you can accomplish anything without that same recognition? What one action this week can you consciously attach 'insha'Allah' to as a true reminder of your dependence?
?
Consider your biggest goal right now. Have you attached 'insha'Allah' to it with full conviction that its accomplishment is not in your hands? What would change in your anxiety or confidence if you truly lived by Al-Ash'ari's proof that capability is given only at the moment of action? Write down one goal and recommit it to Allah's will.

The Prisoner's Forgetfulness: Divine Will Removes Capacity
Al-Ash'ari uses the prisoner's forgetfulness as evidence against independent human capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the story of the prisoner demonstrates that human capacity is contingent upon God's will and can be removed at any time.

Core Idea
God can remove human capacity at will, as shown by the prisoner's forgetfulness.

Al-Ash'ari begins his argument by citing a Quranic narrative: the story of the prisoner who promised to mention Yusuf to the king but forgot due to Satan. This example illustrates that human capacity (istita'a) is not an inherent, independent power but is entirely subject to God's control. By examining this story, we see that even a sincere intention can be thwarted if God does not will its execution.

Guided Path
1
Read the story in the passage
Read the Arabic passage about the prisoner and Yusuf. Notice the cause: Satan made him forget.
The word 'istita'a' appears in the negative: 'فَلَمْ تَكُنْ لِلنَّاجِي استطاعَةٌ'.
2
Identify the theological point
The lack of capacity is directly linked to divine will. God did not will that the prisoner remember, so he had no capacity to do so.
3
Contrast with independent capacity
If capacity were independent, the prisoner could have remembered regardless. But he couldn't, proving that capacity depends on God.
This refutes the view that humans have autonomous power over their actions.

Source Text

اللُّمَع في الرد على أَهلِ الزَّيْغِ والبدع
أَنْسَى الشيطانُ النَّاجِيَ أن يَذْكُرَ يوسف عند الملكِ، فَلَمْ تَكُنْ
للنَّاجي استطاعَةٌ، أن يذكُرَ أمرَ يُوسفَ للملكِ؛ إذْ كَانَ قَدْ وَعَدَ
يوسف بأن يذكُرَه عند ربه قبل خروجه من السِّجْنِ .
وكان ذلك لتمام مرادِ الله -تعالى- بيُوسفَ إلى الوَقْتِ المعلومِ
الَّذي رأى الملكُ فيه الرُّؤْيَا .
وأيضًا : قول الله تعالى لنبيه عليه السلام : ﴿وَلَا نَقُولَنَّ لِشَيْءٍ
إِنِّي فَاعِلُ ذَلِكَ غَدًا إِلا أَن يَشَاءَ اللهُ ﴾ [الكهف : ٢٣-٢٤] ، فأَمَرَ اللَّهُ
-تعالى- نبيَّه بأنْ لا يُقدِمَ على فعل شيء يقعُ في نفسه ما يَأْتِ، بأنْ يَسْتَثْني في قوله ، فأخبر الله - تعالى - نبيَّه أنْ لا يكونَ قولُك هذا كائنا قبلَ فِعْلِكَ له إلا إن أردتُ أنا ذلك، فسلَّمَ النبيُّ
- صلى الله عليه وسلَّم- لأمرِ اللَّهِ – تعالى .
استشكال على مقارنة الاستطاعة للفعل
وقول موسى عليه السلام: ﴿رَبَّنَا اطْمِسْ عَلَى أَمْوَالِهِمْ وَاشْدُدْ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ فَلَا يُؤْمِنُوا حَتَّى يَرَوُا الْعَذَابَ الْأَلِيمَ﴾ [يونس: 88] فَلَمْ يَقْدِرُوا إِذ رَأَوْا العذابَ المُلْجئ لهم إلى الإيمان أن يُؤْمِنُوا، ولو استَطاعُوا ذلك لآمِنُوا عند معاينتهم لأوّل العذابِ النازلِ بهم .
ومثل ذلك في كتابِ الله -تعالى- كثير، وفيما دلنا به كفاية، ومثله قوله - تعالى -: ﴿إِلَّا قَوْمَ يُونُسَ لَمَّا ءَامَنُوا﴾ [يونس: 98]
Al-Luma' in refutation of the people of deviation and innovation. Satan made the saved prisoner forget to mention Yusuf to the king, so the saved one had no capacity (istita'a) to mention Yusuf's matter to the king, since he had promised Yusuf to mention him before his lord before leaving prison. And that was for the completion of Allah's will concerning Yusuf until the appointed time when the king saw the vision. And also: the saying of Allah, the Exalted, to His Prophet, peace be upon him: 'And never say of anything, "Indeed, I will do that tomorrow," except [when adding], "If Allah wills."' [al-Kahf: 23-24]. So Allah, the Exalted, commanded His Prophet not to proceed with an action that occurs in his mind in the future, except by making an exception (istithna) in his statement. So Allah informed His Prophet that your statement would not be before your action unless I will that. So the Prophet submitted to the command of Allah, the Exalted. Objection concerning the comparison of capacity to action. And the saying of Musa, peace be upon him: 'Our Lord, obliterate their wealth and harden their hearts so that they will not believe until they see the painful punishment.' [Yunus: 88] So they were not able, when they saw the compelling punishment, to believe. And if they had capacity (istata'u) for that, they would have believed when they witnessed the first descending punishment. And similar examples in the Book of Allah, the Exalted, are many, and what He has guided us with is sufficient. And likewise His saying, the Exalted: 'Except the people of Yunus when they believed.' [Yunus: 98]
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a proof (istidlal) from Quranic evidence, and it also addresses an objection (istishkal). The author presents two main arguments to demonstrate that human capacity (istita'a) is not independent but subject to God's will. First, the story of the prisoner who promised to mention Yusuf to the king: Satan made him forget, so he lacked the capacity to fulfill his promise. This shows that Allah can remove capacity at will. Then, the command to say 'In sha Allah' indicates that no action occurs without Allah's will. The second part is a specific objection concerning the comparison of capacity to action: the author cites the prayer of Musa against Pharaoh's people, where they were unable to believe even when faced with compelling punishment—thus they had no capacity to believe at that moment. The author concludes that such examples are abundant in the Quran, and then mentions the exception of the people of Yunus as a further case. The passage follows a logical sequence: first establishing the principle, then defending it against a potential objection.

Key Terms
استطاعة
الناجي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans always have the capacity to do what they intend to do.
Correction: The prisoner intended to mention Yusuf but could not because God did not will it, showing capacity is not always present.

Checkpoint
Why did the prisoner fail to mention Yusuf to the king?
A) He chose not to mention him.
B) Satan made him forget.
C) He was afraid of the king.
D) Yusuf asked him not to.

Key Takeaway
The prisoner’s forgetfulness proves that human capacity is not independent but is subject to God’s will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever found yourself unable to do a good deed that you had sincerely intended? How does this passage challenge your assumption that it was purely your own failure or lack of effort?
?
If God can remove your capacity to do even a simple act like remembering a promise, how should that reshape your daily reliance on your own abilities? What one thing will you start asking God for help with today?
?
Are there promises you have made to others that you have forgotten or failed to fulfill? Knowing that the prisoner's forgetfulness was part of God's plan, how can you seek divine assistance for even the smallest commitments you make?

The Command to Say 'In sha Allah': Actions Depend on God's Will
Al-Ash'ari uses the command to say 'In sha Allah' to prove actions depend on God's will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic command to say 'In sha Allah' establishes that no action can occur without God's will, thereby refuting independent human capacity.

Core Idea
Saying 'In sha Allah' affirms that all actions are subject to divine will.

Al-Ash'ari presents another Quranic proof: the command to the Prophet to say 'If Allah wills' when planning any future action. This instruction ties the occurrence of an action directly to God's will. By analyzing this verse, we see that human capacity to act is not sufficient; God's will must precede any action.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its explanation
Read the Arabic passage containing the verse from Surah al-Kahf and Al-Ash'ari's commentary on it.
The verse commands: 'إِلَّا أَن يَشَاءَ اللهُ' — 'except if Allah wills.'
2
Understand the implication
The command implies that no action is realized unless Allah wills it. The Prophet submitted to this command, showing his acknowledgment that his own will is not decisive.
3
Connect to capacity
If human capacity were independent, there would be no need to condition actions on God's will. The verse proves that capacity is effective only when God wills the action.
This refutes the idea that humans have autonomous power.

Moses' Prayer and the People of Yunus: Inability Despite Motivation
Al-Ash'ari responds to an objection using Moses' prayer and the people of Yunus as evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the examples of Moses' prayer against Pharaoh's people and the people of Yunus show that even when circumstances compel belief, humans may lack the capacity to do so without God's will.

Core Idea
Even compelling circumstances cannot produce faith without God granting capacity.

Al-Ash'ari addresses an objection by citing the prayer of Moses against Pharaoh's people. Despite seeing painful punishment, they were unable to believe. Similarly, the people of Yunus are mentioned as an exception. These examples reinforce that human capacity is not intrinsic; even when external factors strongly motivate an action, God may withhold the ability to perform it.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and examples
Read the Arabic passage starting with 'استشكال على مقارنة الاستطاعة للفعل' and the following verses.
The objection is about comparing capacity to action; Al-Ash'ari responds with examples.
2
Analyze the example of Pharaoh's people
Moses prayed that they would not believe until they see painful punishment. When they saw it, they still could not believe, proving they lacked capacity at that moment.
The text says 'فَلَمْ يَقْدِرُوا إِذ رَأَوْا العذابَ' — 'they were not able when they saw the punishment.'
3
Consider the exception of Yunus' people
The people of Yunus are mentioned as a contrast: they believed when they saw punishment. This shows that belief occurs only when God wills and grants capacity.
The phrase 'إِلَّا قَوْمَ يُونُسَ' indicates an exception that proves the rule.

?

?
The proof shows that capacity to act is not automatic; it is given by God. Is there a good deed you have been putting off, assuming you can just do it when you feel ready? What would it mean to ask God for the capacity to do it now?

Refuting the Objection: Ability Does Not Precede Action
Refutes an objection about ability to believe using Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari school refutes the objection that ability precedes action by using Quranic examples.

Core Idea
The Quran shows that ability does not precede action; God's will is decisive.

In this passage, Imam al-Ash'ari addresses a key objection to his position on the relationship between ability and action. The objector argues from the story of Moses and Pharaoh that if ability were not prior, they would have believed. Al-Ash'ari counters by showing that they were prevented by God. Let's examine the argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the objection and the response.
2
Identify the key Quranic verse
Verse 88 of Surah Yunus is central to the argument.
3
Understand the logic
The objector claims that if they could believe, they would have; Al-Ash'ari says they were unable.
4
Note the broader implication
Many Quranic verses support that ability is given at the moment of action, not before.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استشكال على مقارنة الاستطاعة للفعل
وقول موسى عليه السلام: ﴿رَبَّنَا اطْمِسْ عَلَى أَمْوَالِهِمْ وَاشْدُدْ عَلَى قُلُوبِهِمْ فَلا يُؤْمِنُوا حَتَّى يَرَوُا الْعَذَابَ الْأَلِيمَ﴾ [يونس: 88] فلم يَقْدِرُوا إذ رَأَوُا الْعَذَابَ الْمُلْجِئَ لَهُمْ إِلَى الْإِيْمَانِ أَنْ يُؤْمِنُوا، وَلَوِ اسْتَطَاعُوا ذَلِكَ لَآمَنُوا عِنْدَ مُعَايَنَتِهِمْ لِأَوَّلِ الْعَذَابِ النَّازِلِ بِهِمْ. وَمِثْلُ ذَلِكَ فِي كِتَابِ اللهِ تَعَالَى كَثِيرٌ، وَفِيمَا دَلَّنَا بِهِ كِفَايَةٌ، وَمِثْلُهُ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿إِلَّا قَوْمَ يُونُسَ لَمَّا آمَنُوا﴾ [يونس: 98].
Objection regarding the comparison of ability to action. And the saying of Moses, peace be upon him: 'Our Lord, obliterate their wealth and harden their hearts so that they will not believe until they see the painful punishment.' [Yunus: 88] So they were not able, when they saw the punishment compelling them to faith, to believe. And if they had been able to do so, they would have believed when they witnessed the first of the punishment descending upon them. And similar to that in the Book of God, Exalted, is much, and in what He has indicated to us is sufficient. And similar to it is His saying, Exalted: 'Except the people of Yunus when they believed.' [Yunus: 98]
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the claim that ability (istita'a) precedes action. The objector uses the verse where Moses prays for Pharaoh's people to be prevented from believing until they see the painful punishment. The argument is that when the punishment came, they were unable to believe, even though they witnessed it. If they had ability before the action, they would have believed at that moment. The author then notes that many similar examples exist in the Quran, such as the people of Yunus who believed when they saw the punishment but it did not benefit them. This refutes the idea that ability is prior to action.

Key Terms

الفعل
الإيمان
العذاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the verse proves ability before action because they could have believed if they wanted, but the point is that they were prevented by God's will.
Correction: The verse shows that they were unable to believe because God hardened their hearts; ability is not prior but given at the moment of action.

Checkpoint

A) Because they lacked the ability to believe even though they wanted to.
B) Because God prevented them from believing at that time, and they did not have the ability to believe.
C) Because they were not given the choice to believe.
D) Because they were not sincere.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari argument uses Quranic examples to show that ability is not prior to action; rather, God's will determines when one can act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The people of Pharaoh saw clear evidence and still could not believe because God hardened their hearts. Is there any area in your life where you are relying on your own willpower instead of humbly asking God to grant you the ability to obey? What specific step will you take today to acknowledge your dependence on Him?
?
This lesson teaches that ability is not prior to action but is given by God at the moment of action. How does this change your understanding of your daily shortcomings in worship? Will you start your next prayer by asking God for the ability to pray with true presence of heart?

Refuting Ability Before Action from Shu'ayb's Daughter
Refutes al-Jubba'i's argument using context of the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why al-Ash'ari refutes al-Jubba'i's claim that the daughter of Shu'ayb's statement proves ability (istita'a) exists before action.

Core Idea
The daughter praised Moses after seeing his actions, not before.

Al-Jubba'i used a Quranic verse to argue that ability exists before action. He cited the daughter of Shu'ayb calling Moses strong and trustworthy. But al-Ash'ari points out a critical flaw: she only praised him after witnessing his deeds. Let's see how this refutes the claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note how al-Jubba'i's argument is presented and then refuted.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لم تعرف موسى من قبل'.
2
Identify al-Jubba'i's argument
Al-Jubba'i claimed that the daughter's statement indicates that Moses had ability before performing any tasks. How did he use the verse to support this?
3
Understand al-Ash'ari's refutation
Al-Ash'ari argues that she did not know Moses before his actions; her praise came after seeing his strength and trustworthiness. This shows ability is known through action, not before it.
The key is the timing: observation preceded praise.
4
Reflect on the logic
Consider why this refutation works. If ability were before action, the daughter could have known it without seeing the action. But she needed to see the action to judge.
This aligns with the Ash'ari position that ability is simultaneous with action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

36- Issue. And whoever asks about the saying of the daughter of Shu'ayb to her father: 'O my father, hire him. Indeed, the best of those you hire is the strong and trustworthy.' That is because she did not know Moses before his removal of the stone that he removed, and his drawing with the bucket that he drew. Rather, it was when she witnessed his strength, power, and trustworthiness. That is because when she returned to him the second time, she said to him: 'Indeed, my father invites you.' [Al-Qasas: 25]

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection raised by al-Jubba'i who cited the verse where the daughter of Shu'ayb praises Moses as strong and trustworthy to argue that ability (istita'a) exists before the action. The author refutes this by pointing out that the daughter did not know Moses prior to seeing him perform the actions (removing the stone and drawing water). Her judgment was based on her direct observation of his strength and trustworthiness during those actions. Therefore, this does not prove that ability precedes action; rather, it proves that ability is known through the action itself. The author expresses astonishment at al-Jubba'i's reasoning.

Reconciling Creation for Worship and Hell
Ash'ari answers objection about verse 51:56 and reconciles with 7:179

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari resolves the apparent contradiction between two Quranic verses about the purpose of creation.

Core Idea
Not all are created to worship—God wills worship for some, hell for others.

This lesson examines a key objection raised against the doctrine of imposing what cannot be borne. The objector points to verse 51:56 which states that Allah created jinn and humans only to worship Him. Yet many do not worship. Ash'ari responds by interpreting the verse in light of another verse (7:179) and the concept of divine will. Let's see his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection based on verse 51:56 and understand why it seems problematic.
2
See Ash'ari's interpretation
Notice how Ash'ari reinterprets the lam in 'liya'budun' as indicating divine will for a specific group.
3
Consider supporting evidence
Examine how Ash'ari uses verse 7:179 to support his interpretation.
4
Grasp the resolution
Understand that the Quran does not contradict; God creates some for worship and some for Hell.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومَنْ سأل عن قولِ اللَّهِ -تعالى-: ﴿وَمَا خَلَقْتُ الْجِنَّ وَالْإِنسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونِ ﴾ [الذاريات: ٥٦]؟ قيلَ لَه: المعنى في ذلكَ: أنَّه أراد بعض الجن والإنس وهم العابدونَ للَّه منهم؛ لأنَّ الله -تعالى- قال في موضع آخر: ﴿وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنَا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيرًا مِّنَ الْجِنِّ وَالإِنسِ﴾ [الأعراف: ١٧٩]، والقرآن لا يَتَناقَضُ، فَوَجَبَ أن يكونَ اللَّهُ - تعالى - خَلَقَ لجهنَّم كثيرًا، بالآية التي تَلَوْناها، وأنَّه خَلَقَ بعضهم للعبادة، بقوله: ﴿وَمَا خَلَقْتُ النَّ وَالإِنسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونِ ﴾ [الذاريات: ٥٦] والذين خلقهم لعبادتِه هم الذينَ أَراد أنْ يَعبدوه، وعاقبتهم عبادَتُه.
And whoever asks about the saying of Allah - exalted is He -: 'And I did not create the jinn and humans except to worship Me' [51:56]? It is said to him: The meaning of that is that He intended some of the jinn and humans, and they are the worshipers of Allah among them; because Allah - exalted is He - said in another place: 'And We have certainly created many of the jinn and humans for Hell' [7:179], and the Quran does not contradict, so it is necessary that Allah - exalted is He - created many for Hell, by the verse we have recited, and that He created some for worship, by His saying: 'And I did not create the jinn and humans except to worship Me' [51:56]; and those whom He created for His worship are those whom He willed to worship Him, and their end is His worship.
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The objector cites the verse 'I created the jinn and humans only to worship Me' (51:56) as potentially problematic for the doctrine of imposing what cannot be borne, since it suggests God created all for worship yet many do not worship. Ash'ari answers by interpreting the lam (ل) in 'liya'budun' as indicating divine will (إرادة) rather than a universal causal purpose. He says the meaning is that God intended (أراد) some of the jinn and humans to worship Him, specifically those who actually will worship. This is supported by another verse 'We have created many jinn and humans for Hell' (7:179). Since the Quran does not contradict, God created some for worship and some for Hell by His will. Those created for worship are those whose ultimate outcome (عاقبة) is worship. Thus the objection is resolved: the verse does not imply that all must worship, but that God willed worship for a particular group.

Key Terms
تكليف ما لا يطاق
لام العاقبة
لام الإرادة
العبادة
جهنم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'ما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون' implies that every human is created to worship God, making unbelief a contradiction of God's purpose.
Correction: Ash'ari clarifies that the lam indicates divine will (إرادة) for a specific group, not a universal cause. Not all are created to worship; some are created for Hell.

Checkpoint

B) It indicates divine will for some of them.
C) It indicates a command for all.
D) It indicates a test.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari resolves the apparent contradiction by interpreting the lam in 'liya'budun' as divine will for a specific group, supported by verses showing creation for Hell.
