Ash'ari's Interpretation of 5:103: God Did Not Command Pagan Practices
Ash'ari denies that God commanded pagan practices mentioned in 5:103

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari interprets the verse about bahira, sa'iba, wasila, and hami to deny that God commanded pagan practices, and how this preserves God's right to command what He wills.

Core Idea
The verse denies false attribution, not God's right to command.

This passage addresses a potential objection from Quran 5:103. An opponent might argue that the verse shows God does not impose burdens because it says 'Allah has not appointed...' Ash'ari clarifies that the verse means God did not command or impose these specific pagan practices; rather, the pagans falsely claimed God commanded them. This preserves the principle that God can command what He wills, including what may be considered burdensome.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own wording come through.
The passage is short but dense in meaning.
2
Identify the objection the verse might pose
Consider how someone might use this verse to argue that God does not impose burdens (taklif ma la yutaq). Where in the verse might that objection come from?
The phrase 'ما جعل الله' could be misinterpreted as a blanket denial.
3
Understand Ash'ari's two denials
Ash'ari specifies two things God did not do: 'لم أفرض' (I did not impose) and 'لم آمر' (I did not command). Notice the order and the choice of words.
These are distinct but related: imposing a practice as a duty vs. commanding it.
4
Note the false attribution
The pagans claimed that God commanded them. Ash'ari says they lied. So the verse is denying their lie, not denying God's authority.
This is the key move for Ash'ari's argument.
5
Reflect on the implication for divine command
If the verse only denies false attribution, then the possibility of God commanding what is burdensome remains open. Consider why this matters for kalam discussions on taklif.
This connects to broader theological debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومَنْ سألَ عن قوله - تعالى -: مَا جَعَلَ اللَّهُ مِنْ بَحِيرَةٍ وَلَا سَابِبَةٍ وَلَا وَصِيلَةِ وَلَا حَامٍ وَلَكِنَّ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا يَفْتَرُونَ عَلَى اللَّهِ الْكَذِبَ [المائدة: ١٠٣] فالمَعْنَى: إِنِّي لم أَفْرِضْ عليهم ذلك وَلَمْ آمُرْهم به، ولكنَّهُم كَذَبُوا عليَّ، وافتَرَوُا الكَذِبَ في قولهم: إِنِّي أَمَرْتُهم بِهِ.
And whoever asks about His saying - exalted is He -: 'Allah has not appointed [any] bahira or sa'iba or wasila or hami' [5:103], rather the meaning is: I did not impose that upon them nor did I command them with it, but they lied against Allah and fabricated the lie in their saying: 'I commanded them with it.'
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This is a clarification passage. An objector might cite the verse 'Allah has not appointed any bahira or sa'iba or wasila or hami' to argue that God does not impose burdens on people (here referring to pagan animal practices). Ash'ari explains that the meaning of the verse is that God did not impose (أفرض) these practices nor command (آمر) them to do so. Rather, the pagans falsely attributed these commands to God by claiming 'I commanded them with it.' Thus the verse is a denial of a false attribution, not a denial of God's right to impose what cannot be borne. Ash'ari thereby preserves the possibility of such imposition.

Key Terms
بحيرة
سائبة
وصيلة
حام
افتراء
تكليف ما لا يطاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might interpret the verse as God's prohibition of these practices or as a general denial of God imposing any obligations.
Correction: Ash'ari stresses it is about what God ordained/commanded, not about prohibition per se. The verse denies the false attribution, not God's right to command burdensome duties.

Checkpoint
How does Ash'ari interpret the verse 'ما جعل الله من بحيرة ولا سائبة ولا وصيلة ولا حام'?
A) God forbade those practices.
B) God did not command or impose those practices, and the pagans falsely attributed them to Him.
C) God permitted those practices.
D) God was unaware of those practices.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari clarifies that the verse 5:103 does not deny God's right to command burdensome obligations; it denies that God commanded those specific pagan practices, revealing the pagans' lie.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Quranic Proof for Imposing What Cannot Be Borne
Ash'ari cites two Quranic proofs for the permissibility of imposing what cannot be borne.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari uses two Quranic examples to demonstrate that God can validly command what a person is unable to do.

Core Idea
God's command does not depend on the creature's ability.

Imam al-Ash'ari now turns to the Quran to provide scriptural support for the controversial doctrine that God may impose what cannot be borne. He cites two explicit incidents where beings were commanded to do something they could not perform. This passage shows that the Ash'ari position is not merely rational speculation but is grounded in divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation. Let the structure of the argument become clear.
The passage starts with 'الدليل على جواز...' and then lists two examples.
2
Identify the two Quranic examples
Find the first example (angels and names) and the second (prostration in afterlife). Consider how each shows a command beyond the creature's ability at that moment.
The first is from Surah al-Baqarah (2:31), the second refers to Surah al-Qalam (68:42-43).
3
Understand the analogical argument
Ash'ari argues: if God can validly command what cannot be done in the afterlife, then the same is valid in this world. Reflect on why this analogy is considered sound in kalam.
The analogy assumes that the permissibility of such a command is not context-dependent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدَّليلُ على جوازِ تَكْلِيفِ ما لا يُطاقُ مِنَ القرآنِ قولُهُ [تعالى] للملائكة: أَنْتُونِي بِأَسْمَاءِ هَؤُلَاءِ [البقرة: ٣١] يعني: أسماء الخَلْقِ، وَهُمْ لَا يعلمون ذلك، ولا يقدرون عليه. وأيضًا: فقَدْ أَخْبَرَ أَنَّهم ويدعون إِلَى السُّجُودِ فَلَا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ، فإذا جازَ تكليفه إيَّاهُم في الآخرةِ ما لَا يُطيقونَ، جَازَ ذلكَ في الدُّنيا.
And the evidence from the Quran for the permissibility of imposing what cannot be borne is His saying [exalted is He] to the angels: 'Inform Me of the names of these' [2:31] meaning: the names of the creatures, and they did not know that and were not able to do it. And also: Indeed He informed that they are called to prostrate but they cannot, so if it is permissible for Him to impose upon them in the afterlife what they cannot bear, then that is permissible in this world.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This is a proof passage. Ash'ari provides two Quranic examples to demonstrate that God can impose what cannot be borne (تكليف ما لا يطاق). First, He commanded the angels to inform Him of the names of things (البقرة 2:31), but they did not know and were unable to comply; yet it was a valid command. Second, in the afterlife, some will be called to prostrate but will be unable to do so (referring to Quran 68:42-43). Since God imposes this on beings in the afterlife who cannot do it, it is permissible for Him to do the same in this world. The argument is analogical: if it is valid in one context, it is valid in another.

Key Terms
تكليف ما لا يطاق
الملائكة
السجود
الآخرة
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that the angels could have known the names if they had been taught, so the command was not truly impossible.
Correction: Ash'ari's point is that at the moment of command, the angels lacked the ability; the command was to do something they could not do at that time, regardless of whether they could later learn.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic example does Ash'ari use to support the permissibility of imposing what cannot be borne?
A) God commanding the angels to inform Him of the names of things, which they did not know.
B) God commanding Moses to speak to Pharaoh.
C) God commanding Ibrahim to sacrifice his son.
D) God commanding the Prophet to pray at night.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari uses two Quranic examples to prove that God can validly command what cannot be borne, establishing the doctrine on scriptural grounds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you come across a command of Allah that feels beyond your strength, do you use it as an excuse to give up or as a call to rely on His help? How does this lesson challenge the way you respond to difficult obligations?
?
The angels were perfect in obedience yet God commanded them something they could not do. How does this affect your trust in God's wisdom when He commands you something you do not understand or cannot measure up to?
?
On the Day of Judgment, the disbelievers will long to prostrate but will be unable. What does that tell you about the urgency of obeying Allah now, while you still have the ability? Is there any act of obedience you are postponing that you might not be able to perform later?

Reconciling Creation for Hell and for Worship
Al-Ash'ari reconciles the verses on creation for Hell and for worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari reconciles the two Quranic verses about creation for Hell and creation for worship without contradiction.

Core Idea
Allah creates some for Hell and some for worship, both by His will.

Al-Ash'ari addresses an apparent contradiction between two Quranic verses: one saying Allah created many for Hell, another saying He created all for worship. He shows that the Qur'an does not contradict itself and that both verses are true when understood properly. This lesson explores his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to get the author's argument.
Notice the two Quranic verses cited.
2
Identify the two verses
Find the verse about Hell (Al-A'raf 7:179) and the one about worship (Adh-Dhariyat 51:56).
3
Understand the principle
Al-Ash'ari states that the Qur'an does not contradict. This is the key to reconciliation.
The principle is explicitly stated.
4
See the resolution
The author concludes that some are created for Hell and some for worship, and those for worship are those He willed to worship.
5
Reflect on the outcome
The final outcome of the worship-created is worship, aligning with divine will.
Consider how this preserves both divine justice and mercy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العابدونَ للَّه منهم؛ لأنَّ الله -تعالى- قال في موضع آخر : ﴿وَلَقَدْ ذَرَأْنَا لِجَهَنَّمَ كَثِيرًا مِّنَ الْجِنِّ وَالإِنسِ [الأعراف: ۱۷۹]، والقرآن لا يَتَناقَضُ، فَوَجَبَ أن يكونَ اللَّهُ - تعالى - خَلَقَ لجهنَّم كثيرًا، بالآية التي تَلَوْناها، وأنَّه خَلَقَ بعضهم للعبادة، بقوله: ﴿وَمَا خَلَقْتُ النَّ وَالإِنسَ إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُونِ ﴾ [الذاريات : ٥٦] والذين خلقهم لعبادتِه هم الذينَ أَراد أنْ يَعبدوه ، وعاقبتهم عبادَتُه .
Those who worship Allah among them, because Allah - exalted - said in another place: 'And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and mankind' [Al-A'raf: 179], and the Qur'an does not contradict. So it is necessary that Allah - exalted - created many for Hell, by the verse we recited, and that He created some of them for worship, by His statement: 'And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me' [Adh-Dhariyat: 56]. And those whom He created for His worship are the ones He willed to worship Him, and their final outcome is His worship.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a reconciliation of two apparently conflicting verses. The author establishes that the Qur'an does not contradict itself. Therefore, the verse that says Allah created many for Hell (Al-A'raf 7:179) and the verse that says He created humans and jinn only to worship Him (Adh-Dhariyat 51:56) must be harmonized. The author argues that both are true: Allah created some for Hell and some for worship. Those created for worship are precisely those whom He willed to worship Him, and their ultimate end is worship. This resolves the tension between divine will and divine justice.

Misconception: Some think that if God creates for Hell, He does not will worship for them.
Correction: The author shows that both creation for Hell and creation for worship are aspects of divine will; those created for worship are the ones He willed to worship.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari shows that Allah creates some for Hell and some for worship, and those for worship are the ones He wills to worship, thus both verses are true without contradiction.

Divine Will Does Not Wrong Anyone
Ashari explains the meaning of verses denying Allah's will to do injustice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ashari reconciles verses denying Allah's will to do injustice with the existence of human wrongdoing.

Core Idea
Allah wills justice for Himself but permits mutual injustice among people.

A common objection arises from verses like 'Allah does not intend injustice for the servants.' How can this be true when people clearly wrong each other? Ashari's answer is subtle: Allah never wills to be unjust Himself, but He may will that people treat each other unjustly. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the first objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage for the first objection and its translation. Notice how the question is framed and the key phrase 'لم يرد أن يظلمهم'.
2
Understand the distinction
Ashari distinguishes between Allah's own act (not willing injustice) and His willing that people commit injustice among themselves. This resolves the apparent conflict.
This distinction preserves Allah's justice while acknowledging human actions.
3
Reflect on the broader principle
Consider how this principle applies to other verses about divine will and evil. Ashari's approach avoids attributing injustice to Allah.
This is a key tenet of Sunni kalam on qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ سَأَلَ عَنْ قَوْلِهِ -تَعَالَى-: ﴿وَمَا اللَّهُ يُرِيدُ ظُلْمًا لِلْعِبَادِ﴾ [غَافِر: 31]، ﴿وَمَا اللَّهُ يُرِيدُ ظُلْمًا لِلْعَالَمِينَ﴾ [آل عِمْرَانَ: 108]. فَالْمَعْنَى فِي ذَلِكَ: أَنَّهُ لَمْ يُرِدْ أَنْ يَظْلِمَهُمْ، وَإِنْ كَانَ أَرَادَ أَنْ يَتَظَالَمُوا. وَمَنْ سَأَلَ عَنْ قَوْلِهِ -تَعَالَى-: سَيَقُولُ الَّذِينَ أَشْرَكُوا لَوْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ مَا أَشْرَكْنَا وَلَا آبَاؤُنَا [الْأَنْعَامِ: 148] إِلَى قَوْلِهِ: كَذَلِكَ كَذَّبَ الَّذِينَ مِنْ قَبْلِهِمْ [الْأَنْعَامِ: 148]. فَالْجَوَابُ: أَنَّهُمْ قَالُوا ذَلِكَ عَلَى طَرِيقِ الِاسْتِهْزَاءِ، وَلَمْ يَقُولُوهُ عَلَى جِهَةِ الِاعْتِقَادِ. فَأَكْذَبَهُمْ فِي قَوْلِهِمِ الَّذِي لَمْ يَكُونُوا لَهُ مُعْتَقِدِينَ، كَمَا أَكْذَبَ الْمُنَافِقِينَ فِي قَوْلِهِمْ: نَشْهَدُ إِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ [الْمُنَافِقُونَ: 1] عَلَى طَرِيقِ الِاسْتِهْزَاءِ. فَقَالَ اللَّهُ -تَعَالَى-: ﴿وَاللَّهُ يَعْلَمُ إِنَّكَ لَرَسُولُهُ وَاللَّهُ يَشْهَدُ إِنَّ الْمُنَافِقِينَ لَكَذِبُونَ﴾ [الْمُنَافِقُونَ: 1].
And whoever asks about His saying, exalted is He: 'And Allah does not intend injustice for the servants' (Ghafir 31), 'And Allah does not intend injustice for the worlds' (Aal-e-Imran 108). The meaning of that is: that He did not intend to wrong them, even if He intended that they wrong each other. And whoever asks about His saying, exalted is He: 'The polytheists will say: If Allah had willed, we would not have associated [others] nor our fathers' (Al-An'am 148) up to His saying: 'Thus did those before them deny' (Al-An'am 148). The answer: that they said that by way of mockery, and they did not say it as a matter of belief. So He declared them false regarding their statement which they did not believe, just as He declared the hypocrites false in their saying: 'We bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah' (Al-Munafiqun 1) by way of mockery. So Allah, exalted is He, said: 'And Allah knows that you are His Messenger, and Allah bears witness that the hypocrites are liars' (Al-Munafiqun 1).
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents two objections with their answers. The first objection questions verses that state Allah does not will injustice. Ashari explains that Allah does not will to be unjust Himself, but He may will that people treat each other unjustly—meaning He permits or creates the actions of wrongdoing. The second objection concerns the polytheists' argument from predestination: 'If Allah had willed, we would not have associated partners.' Ashari refutes this by arguing that the polytheists did not genuinely believe this; they said it mockingly. He compares them to hypocrites who falsely claimed to believe in Muhammad. Thus, Allah declared them liars in their statement because they did not hold it as a conviction. Therefore, the verse is a response to mockery, not a valid theological argument.

ظلم

A) Allah does not will any injustice at all.
B) Allah does not will to wrong them Himself.
C) Allah does not will that people wrong each other.
D) Allah wills all injustice.

Key Takeaway
Allah never wills to be unjust, but He may will that people treat each other unjustly, which does not contradict His justice.

?
The verse says Allah does not intend injustice for the servants. What does that mean for your relationship with Allah when you feel mistreated? Are you willing to believe that Allah never wrongs you, even when others do? How will that belief change your response to hardship?

Polytheists' Predestination Excuse Refuted
Ashari refutes the polytheists' predestination excuse as insincere mockery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ashari's refutation of the polytheists' argument that their shirk was predetermined by Allah's will.

Core Idea
The polytheists' claim 'if Allah willed, we would not have associated partners' was insincere mockery, not genuine belief.

The polytheists once argued that their idolatry was unavoidable because Allah willed it. Ashari responds by showing that they did not truly believe this—they said it mockingly. This lesson examines how Allah declared them liars, just as He did with hypocrites who falsely professed faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the polytheists' statement and Allah's response
Read the Arabic passage for the second objection. Note the phrase 'على طريق الاستهزاء' which is key.
2
Understand the comparison with hypocrites
Ashari compares the polytheists to the hypocrites who said 'We bear witness you are the Messenger of Allah' mockingly. Allah declared them liars because they did not believe it.
This shows that the verse is about sincerity, not about the truth of the statement itself.
3
Grasp the theological implication
The polytheists' argument is invalid because it was not based on sincere belief. Therefore, it cannot be used as a defense for shirk.
This refutes the idea that the Qur'an endorses predestination as an excuse for disbelief.

Inherence of Obedience and Disobedience: A Dialectical Proof
Imam Ash'ari engages in a dialectical exchange on the inherence of obedience and disobedience in human actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari dialectical argument that obedience and disobedience inhere in human actions, and how the author refutes the objectors' denial of inherence by showing consistency with their own views on movement and prayer.

Core Idea
The inherence of obedience is proven by the same logic that proves the inherence of movement.

This passage presents a rigorous dialectical exchange on whether obedience and disobedience inhere in the human agent. The objectors initially deny inherence for submission, but the author forces them to accept that the same reasoning that applies to movement and prayer applies to obedience. Through a series of logical concessions, the author establishes that a person can be obedient or disobedient through inherence, yet still responsible for performing the act.

Guided Path
1
Read the dialectical exchange carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting each turn in the argument.
The text is cut off at the end; the argument continues in later lessons.
2
Identify the objectors' initial claim
They say the submissive one is not submissive due to inherence nor performance. The author immediately points to the liar as a counter.
3
Trace the author's analogies
He uses movement, lying, and prayer to show that the objectors already accept inherence for these. Note their concessions.
Each concession builds the argument.
4
Notice the objectors' revision
They distinguish movement inherence from obedience performance. The author turns this against them using prayer.
5
Draw the conclusion
The author asks why they accept inherence for prayer but not for submission/obedience. The passage ends with a pending conclusion.
Think about how the argument would continue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بابُ الكلام في التعديل والتجويرِ

فَإِنْ قَالُوا : لم يَكُنِ الخاضِعُ خَاضِعًا لحلولِ الخُضُوعِ فيه، ولَا لأَنَّه فَعَلَه . قِيلَ لَهُم ذَلِكَ في الكَاذِبِ. ثُمَّ يُقالُ لهم : إِذَا أَمَرَنا الله أن نتحرَّكَ أَفَلَيْسَ جَائِزا أن يجعلنا متحركين؟ فإن قالُوا : نَعَمْ . قِيلَ لهُم : فكذلكَ لَوْ أَمَرَنا بالكَذِبِ لجاز أن يجعلنا كاذبين . ثم يُقالُ لهم : خَبِّرونا : أَلَيْسَ زَعَمْتُم أَنَّ الصَّلَاةَ إِذَا كَانَت كَانَتْ حَرَكَاتٍ، وكانَ المتحرِّكُ مُتحرِّكًا لحلول الحركة فيه، والمُصلِّي مُصلِّيا لحلولِ الصَّلَاةِ فيه؟ فإن قالوا : نَعَمْ . قيلَ لهم : فيَجِبُ إذا أطاعَ الإنسانُ بِفِعل حَرَكَةٍ أَمَرَهُ اللَّهُ - تعالى - بهَا ، أن يكُونَ طائعا ؛ لأنَّ الطَّاعَةَ حَلَّتْهُ، كما أنَّه مُتحرِّك لحلولِ الحركة فيه. فإن قالُوا : نَعَمْ .

قِيلَ لهم : فبَعْضُ الإنسانِ طائِعٌ، وبَعْضُه عاص، إِذَا حَلَّتْه المعصية، ولا بُدَّ مِنْ : نَعَمْ . فيُقالُ لَهُمْ : فما أَنْكَرْتُم أن يَكونَ بَعْضُ الإنسانِ مُتكلّما ، وهو اللّسانُ، وبَعْضُهُ عالما مريدا ، وهو القَلبُ؟ فَإِنْ قالُوا : الحَرَكةُ إذا كانَتْ طاعةً، فالمُتحرِّكُ مُتحرِّك لحلولِ الحَرَكَةِ فيه، وليس الطَّائعُ طائعا لحلولِ الطاعة فيه، بل هو طائع بفعل الطاعة. قيل لهم : ما أنكرتُم : إِنْ كَانَتِ الحركاتُ صَلاةٌ، وكانَ المُتحرِّكُ متحركًا لحلولِ الحَرَكَةِ فيه، فالمُصلِّي مصل ؛ لأنه فَعَلَ الصلاة لا لأنَّها حَلَّتْه . فَإِنْ أَجَابُوا إلى ذَلِكَ . قيلَ لهم : فإذَا أَمَرَنا أن نُصلّي، ولم يَجُزْ أن يُصلِّي هُوَ، فَيَلْزَمُ :
Chapter on discourse regarding modification and evaluation. If they say: The submissive one is not submissive due to inherence of submission in him, nor because he performed it. It is said to them: That [applies] in the case of the liar. Then it is said to them: When God commanded us to move, is it not possible that He makes us moving? If they say: Yes. It is said to them: Similarly, if He commanded us to lie, it would be possible that He makes us liars. Then it is said to them: Inform us: Did you not claim that prayer, when it exists, consists of movements, and the mover is moving due to inherence of movement in him, and the pray-er is praying due to inherence of prayer in him? If they say: Yes. It is said to them: Then it follows that if a person obeys by performing a movement which God – exalted – commanded him, he is obedient because obedience inheres in him, just as he is moving due to inherence of movement in him. If they say: Yes. It is said to them: So part of a person is obedient and part disobedient, when disobedience inheres in him, and it must be: Yes. Then it is said to them: What prevents you from [saying] that part of a person is speaking, which is the tongue, and part of him is knowing, willing, which is the heart? Then if they say: The movement, when it is obedience, the mover is moving due to inherence of movement in him, but the obedient one is not obedient due to inherence of obedience in him; rather he is obedient by performing the act of obedience. It is said to them: What prevents you: If the movements are prayer, and the mover is moving due to inherence of movement in him, then the pray-er is praying because he performed the prayer, not because it inhered in him. Then if they concede to that. It is said to them: So when He commands us to pray, and it is not permissible that He Himself prays, then it follows: ...
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical proof (objection-and-answer). The author presents a series of exchanges on whether attributes like obedience, disobedience, submission, and lying inhere in the human subject. The objectors initially claim that a person is not called submissive due to the inherence of submission, nor because he performed it. The author responds that the same logic applies to the liar, implying inconsistency. He then builds a case using the example of commanded movement: if God commands movement, He can make us moving; similarly for lying. Next, he turns to prayer: the objectors accept that prayer consists of movements and that the mover is moving due to inherence of movement, and the pray-er is praying due to inherence of prayer. The author argues that if a person obeys a commanded movement, he is obedient due to inherence of obedience, just as movement inheres. The objectors agree. Then the author extends the argument: part of a person can be obedient and part disobedient if obedience/disobedience inheres, and he asks why they deny that part of a person can be speaking (the tongue) and part knowing/willing (the heart). At this point, the objectors revise their position: they distinguish between movement and obedience. They say that for movement, the mover is moving due to inherence, but the obedient person is not obedient due to inherence; rather, he is obedient by performing the act of obedience. The author then uses the objectors' own logic against them: if movements are prayer, and the mover is moving due to inherence, yet the pray-er is praying because he performed the prayer, not because prayer inheres, then why not apply the same to obedience? The objectors concede this point. Finally, the author draws a conclusion that if God commands us to pray and it is not permissible that He Himself prays, then something follows (the text cuts off). The argument essentially forces the objectors to accept that human actions are acquired by the human agent even though God creates them, but the passage focuses on the inherence vs. performance distinction.

Key Terms
التعديل
التجوير
الخاضع
الخضوع
الكاذب
الطاعة
المعصية
الصلاة
الحركة
الحلول
الطائع
العاصي
المصلّي
فعل الطاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ash'ari view denies human agency entirely; obedience is solely by God's creation without human role.
Correction: The author shows that a person is called obedient because he performs the act of obedience, preserving human responsibility despite inherence.

Checkpoint
According to the objectors' final position in this passage, what makes a person obedient?
A) The inherence of obedience in him
B) His performing the act of obedience
C) Both inherence and performance
D) God's direct action

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari position upholds that while God creates actions, human beings are truly agents through performance, and obedience/disobedience inhere in them in a way consistent with other attributes like movement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you truly feel that the disobedience inheres in you, or do you think of it as merely an external action you performed? How does this passage challenge you to reconsider the nature of your own moral states?
?
If obedience and disobedience inhere in you like movement, then your character is shaped by repeated acts. What one act of obedience today could you perform that you would most want to become inherent in your soul?
?
The objectors tried to separate obedience from action, claiming it is just performance. But the author argued they are inseparable. In your life, do you ever separate your inner state from your outer actions? How can you align them starting now?

Divine Decree
beginner
4 min
Actions of Servants: God Creates, Humans Acquire
The author affirms that all actions are from God, while acquisition is from creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari distinction between divine creation of actions and human acquisition.

Core Idea
Actions are created by God; humans acquire them.

This concise passage from Imam al-Ash'ari lays the cornerstone of the Ash'ari position on human actions. Before delving into the complexities of qadar, one must grasp this foundational distinction: God alone creates actions, while humans acquire them. This one sentence defines the middle path between extremes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage Carefully
Read the Arabic phrase and its translation. Notice the concise structure: a negation ('actions belong to God, not to creation') followed by an affirmation ('and acquisition belongs to creation').
The passage is only one sentence, but it carries a profound doctrinal distinction.
2
Identify the Two Key Terms
Focus on 'أفعال' (actions) and 'اكتساب' (acquisition). Understand that 'actions' refers to the very existence of the act, while 'acquisition' is the human role of earning or acquiring that act.
These terms are central to Ash'ari theology.
3
Understand the Negation and Affirmation
The negation 'لا للخلق' explicitly denies that actions are created by creatures. The affirmation 'والاكتساب للخلق' asserts that humans do have a genuine role—acquisition—without creating.
This refutes both the Mu'tazila (who say humans create) and the Jabriyya (who deny human agency).
4
Reflect on the Balanced Doctrine
Ask yourself: Why did Imam al-Ash'ari choose this wording? The dual statement preserves divine omnipotence (actions from God) while upholding human moral responsibility (acquisition by humans).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[أفعال العباد]
ويعتقد أن الأفعال لِلَّهِ -تعالى- لا للخلق، والاكتساب للخلق :
[Actions of servants] And he believes that actions belong to God, exalted, not to creation, and acquisition belongs to creation.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This brief passage encapsulates the Ash'ari position on human actions: the actual creation of actions is from God alone, while humans have an aspect of acquisition (كسب). This distinguishes the Ash'ari view from both the Mu'tazila (who attribute actions entirely to humans) and the Jabriyya (who deny human agency entirely). The term 'الاكتساب' is key: humans acquire the action, but God creates it.

Key Terms
أفعال العباد
اكتساب
خلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans are completely passive and have no role in their actions.
Correction: Imam al-Ash'ari affirms that humans acquire actions, which gives them moral responsibility. The term 'acquisition' indicates a genuine human involvement, even though the act's existence comes from God.

Checkpoint
To whom does the author attribute the actual creation of actions?
A) To the creation
B) To God
C) To both equally
D) To chance

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari position balances divine omnipotence and human responsibility by attributing creation to God and acquisition to humans.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own actions today, how does knowing that God creates them while you only acquire them change your sense of pride in your good deeds? Are you tempted to feel self-sufficient, or does it drive you to thank Allah more?
?
The Ash'ari position says you acquire, but God creates. How does this shape your understanding of your responsibility for your sins? Does it make you more inclined to repent and seek forgiveness, knowing you still acquired the sin, or does it make you feel less blame?
?
If every action you performed today was created by Allah, how does that influence your reliance on Him for even the smallest good deed? Will you remember this when you wake up tomorrow and seek His help in your actions?

Divine Decree
intermediate

Divine Decree and Predestination (Qada' wa Qadr)
Explaining divine decree and predestination, emphasizing sovereignty and will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position on divine decree, including the absolute sovereignty of Allah's will and the distinction between His will and His pleasure regarding human actions.

Core Idea
Allah's will is absolute; He ordains all, but disobedience is by His will, not His pleasure.

This passage from Imam al-Ash'ari's Al-Luma presents a dense series of creedal affirmations regarding divine decree (qada') and predestination (qadr). It tackles the difficult theological questions of how to reconcile divine sovereignty with human responsibility and the existence of evil. The passage distinguishes between Allah's will (irāda) and His pleasure (riḍā) to resolve the problem of evil without compromising omnipotence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without translation. Notice the repetition of 'ويعتقد' (and he believes), which structures the creed as a series of affirmations.
The passage uses a concise, almost list-like format.
2
Identify the affirmations about divine sovereignty
The first sentences declare that Allah does what He wills, is not unjust, judges without objection, and brings near/distances without cause.
This establishes the absolute nature of Allah's actions.
3
Unpack the will vs pleasure distinction
Focus on the sentence: 'obedience is by His pleasure, and disobedience is by His will not by His pleasure'. This is a key theological nuance.
This distinction protects Allah from being the author of evil.
4
Reflect on the implications for predestination
Consider how this view of decree (qada') and predestination (qadr) balances divine control and human accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتقد أنه تعالى فعّال لما يريد ، لا يُنسب إلى الظلم . وأنه يحكم في ملكوته كيف يشاء بلا اعتراض، ولا مَرَدَّ لقضائه ولا مُعَقِّب لحكمه . ويعتقد أنه -تعالى- يقرب من يشاء بغير سبب، ويبعد من يشاء كل المحدثات بإرادته وخلقه. إرادته في عباده ما هم فيه، وبرضاه طاعتهم، والمعصية بمراده لا برضاه . ويعتقد أنه يُعطِي ويمنح، ويَدُمُ وَيَمَّدَحُ .
And he believes that He, exalted, is doer of what He wills, not attributed with injustice. And that He judges in His kingdom as He wishes without objection, and there is no repelling His decree nor any revoker of His judgment. And he believes that He, exalted, brings near whomever He wills without cause, and distances whomever He wills, all originated things are by His will and creation. His will in His servants is what they are in, and obedience is by His pleasure, and disobedience is by His will not by His pleasure. And he believes that He gives and bestows, and dispraises and praises.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage outlines core Ash'ari theology on divine decree (qada') and predestination (qadr). It emphasizes divine sovereignty: Allah does what He wills, and is not subject to injustice (as it would imply a limit on His power). His judgment is absolute. The concept of 'bringing near and distancing without cause' underscores that God's actions are not necessitated by any external reason; they are purely by His will. All originated things (كل المحدثات) are by His will and creation. A key distinction is made: obedience occurs with His pleasure (رضا), disobedience occurs by His will (مراد) but not by His pleasure, which addresses the problem of evil and divine will. The final sentence affirms that He gives and withholds, and He both dispraises and praises, indicating that judgment and reward/punishment belong entirely to Him.

Key Terms
القضاء
القدر
الظلم
الملكوت
الإرادة
الرضا
الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That if God wills disobedience, He is its author and pleased with it.
Correction: The passage clearly states that disobedience is by His will but not by His pleasure, meaning He ordains it but disapproves.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does Allah relate to disobedience?
A) He wills it and is pleased with it.
B) He wills it but is not pleased with it.
C) He neither wills nor permits it.
D) He creates it but is unaware of it.

Key Takeaway
Allah's will encompasses all, but His pleasure is only with good; this distinction preserves divine justice while affirming His absolute sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disobey Allah, do you ever excuse yourself by saying 'it was written for me'? How does this passage's distinction between will and pleasure challenge that excuse, and what will you change in your repentance?
?
You claim to submit to Allah's decree, but do you really accept that He brings near or distances without cause? Is there a situation in your life where you resent His decree? How does this passage demand you surrender your complaint?
?
This passage says obedience is by His pleasure. Does your heart find joy in that, or do you sometimes think your obedience earns you favor? How does understanding that His pleasure is the source of obedience shift your gratitude and humility?

Ability (Istita'a) is with the Act
Imam Ash'ari asserts that ability is simultaneous with the act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari position that human ability to act is simultaneous with the act itself, not prior to it.

Core Idea
Human ability rises with the act, not before it.

This lesson focuses on a concise but foundational statement in Ash'ari theology regarding human capacity. Imam Ash'ari affirms that the ability to perform an action occurs at the same moment as the action, challenging the view that ability precedes the act. This principle has profound implications for understanding divine power and human agency.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic statement carefully
Read the Arabic sentence 'ويعتقد أن الاستطاعة مع الفعل' once to grasp its brevity and directness. Notice the key terms.
The word 'مع' (with) is crucial.
2
Understand the literal translation
Review the English translation: 'And he believes that ability (istita'a) is with the act.' Reflect on what 'with' implies about timing.
3
Consider the theological significance
Think about why this statement matters. In Ash'ari theology, it emphasizes that all power is from Allah and human agency is contingent on divine creation of ability at the moment of action.
This distinguishes Ash'ari from Mu'tazilite views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعتقد أن الاستطاعة مع الفعل.
And he believes that ability (istita'a) is with the act.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This is a brief but important doctrinal statement on the nature of human capacity. The author affirms that the ability to perform an action is simultaneous with the act itself, not prior to it. This is a key position in Ash'ari theology regarding the relationship between human agency and divine power.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة
الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this article, when does the ability (istita'a) occur?
A) Before the act
B) With the act
C) After the act
D) It is eternal

Key Takeaway
In Ash'ari theology, the ability to act is granted by Allah simultaneously with the act itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you wake up each morning and plan your day, do you actually feel that every ability you have—to think, speak, move—is given to you by Allah right at that moment? Or do you subconsciously assume ability is yours permanently? How would conscious awareness of 'ability with the act' change your morning dua?
?
Think of a sin you committed. Did you truly have the ability to avoid it before the moment of action? If ability only comes with the act, then at the moment of sin, Allah gave you ability—but you used it for disobedience. Does this realization deepen your sense of accountability or your need for Allah's grace?
?
Are you currently worried about some future task because you feel you lack the ability now? Based on this lesson, how should you reframe that anxiety? Will you trust that Allah will grant the ability exactly when you need it, not before? What concrete step can you take today to act on that trust?
